## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-007: Method enum

PRD item: JOLT-RS-007 (priority 7, phase01-method-statuscode) — Define Method enum {Get, Post, Put, Patch, Delete, Options, Head} with Display + FromStr in jolt-core. Opens phase01.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 2 passed (from_str_get_is_ok, from_str_invalid_is_err); compiled clean in 6.50s.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 8.60s; no regressions in jolt-macros/jolt-db/jolt-utils/jolt-templates.

Note on harness instructions: the auto-generated task prompt referenced `npm run type-check` and a Bun/Hono server, which are leftovers from a prior Node/TS incarnation of this repo. The current repo is a pure Rust workspace (no package.json, no server/ dir), so verification used `cargo test` + `cargo check --workspace` instead. Future iterations should keep using cargo until/unless package.json reappears.

Key decisions:
- FromStr is case-sensitive against canonical uppercase names (RFC 9110 §9). The PRD verification only tests "GET" → Ok(Get); broader case handling (lowercase/mixed) is not in scope and would silently swallow malformed wire input. If callers need case-insensitive parsing later, they should `s.to_ascii_uppercase()` at the call site rather than baking it into the framework.
- Variant order matches the PRD spec exactly (Get, Post, Put, Patch, Delete, Options, Head) — preserving the spec ordering helps when JOLT-RS-010 writes round-trip tests.
- Added a `Method::as_str() -> &'static str` inherent helper that Display delegates to. This avoids allocating a String just to format the wire name and gives router code a zero-cost path to the canonical bytes. Not in the PRD step list but trivial and load-bearing for future routing work.
- ParseMethodError is a newtype wrapping `String` (the offending input) with std::error::Error + Display impls — gives downstream callers a usable error type without dragging in a thiserror dep yet. Renaming/refactoring later is cheap because it's exposed through `pub use`.
- Re-exported Method + ParseMethodError at the crate root via `pub use method::{Method, ParseMethodError}` — keeps the public API ergonomic (`jolt_core::Method`) while the module structure stays intact for future additions.
- Did NOT yet implement `From<Method> for axum::http::Method` or `serde::{Serialize, Deserialize}` — those are separate concerns and not in JOLT-RS-007's scope. JOLT-RS-009 handles the StatusCode↔axum bridge and may inspire a parallel Method bridge in a later PRD item.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/method.rs (new) — Method enum, Display, FromStr, ParseMethodError, 2 unit tests.
- jolt-core/src/lib.rs — added `pub mod method;` and `pub use method::{Method, ParseMethodError};`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-007 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-008 (StatusCode enum): mirror the Method pattern — enum with named variants + Other(u16) catch-all, in jolt-core/src/status.rs (or status_code.rs). Verification: `from_u16(200) == Ok`, `from_u16(418) == Other(418)`. Note the verification names a `from_u16` constructor (not FromStr), so model it as an inherent associated function `fn from_u16(u16) -> StatusCode` returning the enum directly (no Result needed since Other(_) makes it total).
- JOLT-RS-009 will then add `From<StatusCode> for axum::http::StatusCode` + Display. Same pattern is the natural template for Method↔axum bridging when that PRD item arrives.
- JOLT-RS-010 closes phase01 with comprehensive tests for both Method and StatusCode (round-trips, all variants). Don't pre-write those now — keep JOLT-RS-007/008/009 minimal per the per-item scope rule.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-008: StatusCode enum

PRD item: JOLT-RS-008 (priority 8, phase01-method-statuscode) — Define StatusCode enum with named variants (Ok=200, Created=201, NoContent=204, BadRequest=400, Unauthorized=401, Forbidden=403, NotFound=404, MethodNotAllowed=405, Conflict=409, InternalServerError=500) plus Other(u16) catch-all.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 4 passed (method::tests::from_str_get_is_ok, method::tests::from_str_invalid_is_err, status::tests::from_u16_known_is_named, status::tests::from_u16_unknown_is_other); compiled clean in 0.95s.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.33s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007 — auto-prompt's npm/Bun commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- `from_u16` is a total function returning `StatusCode` directly (not `Result<StatusCode, _>`). The PRD verification says `from_u16(418) == Other(418)`, which only works if Other(_) absorbs unknown codes — making the function infallible. This matches the prior agent's note in the JOLT-RS-007 entry.
- Variant order matches the PRD spec exactly (Ok, Created, NoContent, BadRequest, Unauthorized, Forbidden, NotFound, MethodNotAllowed, Conflict, InternalServerError, Other) for spec traceability and to give JOLT-RS-010 a stable enumeration to round-trip-test.
- Added an `as_u16(&self) -> u16` inherent helper symmetric with `from_u16`. Not in the PRD step list, but it's the natural pair: JOLT-RS-009's `From<StatusCode> for axum::http::StatusCode` will need exactly this lookup, and JOLT-RS-010's round-trip tests (`from_u16(x).as_u16() == x`) will rely on it. Trivial, load-bearing, and avoids JOLT-RS-009 having to add it as undeclared scope creep.
- Did NOT add Display (JOLT-RS-009 owns it) or any axum::http::StatusCode interop. Kept this strictly to the enum + constructor.
- Did NOT include uncommon codes (3xx redirects, 408 Timeout, 429 Too Many Requests, 503 Service Unavailable). The PRD lists exactly ten named variants — adding more would silently broaden the API surface and create ambiguity for JOLT-RS-010's all-variants test. Other(u16) catches everything else cleanly.
- Module file is `src/status.rs` (chose over `status_code.rs` to mirror `method.rs`'s short name; module path is `jolt_core::status::StatusCode`, re-exported as `jolt_core::StatusCode`).
- Re-exported `StatusCode` at the crate root via `pub use status::StatusCode` — same ergonomic pattern as `Method`.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/status.rs (new) — StatusCode enum with 10 named variants + Other(u16), from_u16, as_u16, 2 unit tests.
- jolt-core/src/lib.rs — added `pub mod status;` and `pub use status::StatusCode;`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-008 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-009 (priority 9): `impl From<StatusCode> for axum::http::StatusCode` + `impl Display for StatusCode`. The Display impl can write the numeric code (e.g. "200") or "200 OK"-style — the PRD doesn't say, but axum::http::StatusCode displays as "200 OK" so matching that gives the most user-friendly output. The From impl is mechanical: `axum::http::StatusCode::from_u16(self.as_u16()).expect("StatusCode variants are all valid HTTP codes")` — Other(u16) values from outside the standard 100-599 range would panic, which is acceptable since constructing one of those would be the bug.
- JOLT-RS-010 (priority 10): comprehensive tests. Suggested coverage: every named variant round-trips through from_u16/as_u16; every named variant Display-formats correctly; every named variant converts to the correct axum StatusCode; Other(u16) preserves arbitrary codes; Method::from_str round-trips for all 7 verbs.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-009: StatusCode → axum bridge + Display

PRD item: JOLT-RS-009 (priority 9, phase01-method-statuscode) — Implement From<StatusCode> for axum::http::StatusCode and Display for StatusCode.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 7 passed (5 prior + into_axum_status_not_found, display_known_includes_reason_phrase, display_other_with_known_code_uses_reason_phrase); compiled clean in 1.14s.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.38s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007/008 — npm/Bun commands in the auto-prompt don't apply to this Rust workspace. cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- `From<StatusCode> for axum::http::StatusCode` uses `axum::http::StatusCode::from_u16(self.as_u16()).expect(...)`. The expect message names the invariant ("StatusCode variants must encode valid HTTP status numbers"). All ten named variants encode 200/201/204/400/401/403/404/405/409/500 — all in the valid 100..=999 range. Other(u16) values outside that range will panic, which is correct: constructing Other(99) or Other(1000) is a programming bug, not a recoverable runtime error. Documented this implicitly via the expect message rather than wrapping in a TryFrom — a fallible bridge would force every call site to handle an impossible-for-named-variants error.
- `Display for StatusCode` delegates to axum's canonical_reason for the reason phrase. This matches axum::http::StatusCode's "200 OK" / "404 Not Found" output, which is what users will see in logs and error pages everywhere else in the stack. For Other(u16) codes that lack a canonical reason (or are outside 100..=999), falls back to just the numeric code. This preserves the symmetry that axum gives.
- Did NOT implement Display in terms of as_u16 + a hand-rolled match on canonical reason strings. Letting axum own the reason-phrase mapping means we don't have to update Jolt every time IANA registers a new status code (e.g. the newer 425 Too Early), and we automatically inherit any future axum/http-crate fixes.
- Added three tests aligned with the PRD verification ("StatusCode::NotFound → axum StatusCode 404") plus two adjacent Display tests to lock in the format choice. Other(418) → "418 I'm a teapot" verifies the canonical_reason lookup works for unnamed-but-known codes.
- Pulled `use std::fmt;` at the top of the module rather than fully-qualifying — same style as method.rs.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/status.rs (added From<StatusCode> for axum::http::StatusCode, Display for StatusCode, 3 unit tests).
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-009 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-010 (priority 10, closes phase01): comprehensive tests for Method and StatusCode (all variants, edge cases, conversion round-trips). Suggested coverage: every named StatusCode variant round-trips through from_u16/as_u16; every named StatusCode variant converts to the correct axum::http::StatusCode constant (NOT_FOUND, BAD_REQUEST, etc.); every named StatusCode Display-formats with the expected canonical reason; Other(u16) preserves arbitrary in-range codes through round-trip and Display; Method::from_str round-trips for all 7 verbs (GET/POST/PUT/PATCH/DELETE/OPTIONS/HEAD); Method::as_str/Display match for all 7 verbs. The PRD verification is `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::status_code passes` — note the literal string "tests::status_code", which suggests the agent should add a top-level `mod tests { mod status_code { ... } mod method { ... } }` (or similar) to give the filter a stable target. That's a structural decision worth flagging now.
- After 010, phase02 begins (JOLT-RS-011: Request struct with method, path, headers, query_params, body, cookies fields). This is the first real domain type — likely belongs in jolt-core/src/request.rs.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-010: comprehensive tests for Method and StatusCode

PRD item: JOLT-RS-010 (priority 10, phase01-method-statuscode) — Comprehensive unit tests for Method and StatusCode covering all variants, edge cases, and conversion round-trips. Closes phase01.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::status_code` → 10 passed, 0 failed (9 filtered out by the prefix filter, all from tests::method); compiled clean in 0.99s. Matches the PRD verification command literally.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 19 passed, 0 failed (9 in tests::method, 10 in tests::status_code).
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.33s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007/008/009 — npm/Bun verification commands in the auto-prompt don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Created `jolt-core/src/tests.rs` with `mod method` and `mod status_code` submodules. The PRD verification command filter is `tests::status_code`, which only matches if there's a top-level `tests` module containing a `status_code` submodule. The full test paths are now `tests::method::*` and `tests::status_code::*`, which lets `tests::status_code` filter cleanly to the 10 status-code tests without picking up the 9 method tests. The previous `notes for next iterations` block already flagged this structural choice.
- DELETED the inline `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` blocks from `method.rs` and `status.rs` rather than leaving them alongside the new module. Keeping them would create paths like `method::tests::*` AND `tests::method::*` for what amounts to the same coverage — the new comprehensive tests already subsume every assertion the inline ones made (e.g. `from_str_get_is_ok` is folded into `from_str_round_trips_all_variants`; `into_axum_status_not_found` is folded into `into_axum_status_matches_constants_for_each_named_variant`). One source of truth, no duplicate maintenance.
- Used a `const NAMED_VARIANTS: &[(StatusCode, u16, &str)]` table at the top of each submodule and iterated over it from each test rather than open-coding ten assertions per behavior. This keeps each test small AND ensures that adding a new named variant to `StatusCode` only needs to be added in one place per submodule, not duplicated across every round-trip/display test. Same pattern for `ALL_METHODS` in `tests::method`.
- Method coverage: as_str matches canonical name for all 7 verbs; Display delegates to as_str (so each verb renders correctly); from_str round-trips for all 7 verbs; as_str → from_str is identity; case sensitivity is enforced (lowercase/mixed-case rejected); empty + leading/trailing whitespace rejected; unknown verbs rejected (including HTTP-spec-known-but-unsupported CONNECT/TRACE — documenting that Jolt deliberately does not route these); ParseMethodError preserves offending input in Display; ParseMethodError implements std::error::Error (asserted via the `assert_error<E: std::error::Error>` trick).
- StatusCode coverage: from_u16 maps each named code to the right variant; as_u16 returns the canonical code per variant; from_u16 → as_u16 round-trips; unknown codes (100, 301, 418, 429, 503, 599) round-trip through Other; Other(200) — manually constructed even though 200 has a named variant — still as_u16's to 200 (locks in the "as_u16 reads inner value" invariant); each named variant → axum::http::StatusCode matches the corresponding axum constant (OK/CREATED/NO_CONTENT/BAD_REQUEST/UNAUTHORIZED/FORBIDDEN/NOT_FOUND/METHOD_NOT_ALLOWED/CONFLICT/INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR); Other(418) preserves the code through the axum bridge; Display for each named variant produces the IANA reason phrase ("404 Not Found"); Other(418) → "418 I'm a teapot" via canonical_reason; Other(599) → "599" with no reason (verifies the fallback branch in the Display impl).
- Did NOT add a doctest example to the public API surface — JOLT-RS-010 only calls for unit test coverage, and the public API is already documented via the module doc comments. Doctests would be scope creep.
- Did NOT test the panic in `From<StatusCode> for axum::http::StatusCode` for out-of-range Other(u16) values (e.g. Other(99) or Other(1000)). The panic is documented behavior (the expect message names the invariant) and a `#[should_panic]` test would lock in a panic message that the prior PRD entry (JOLT-RS-009) already chose for diagnostic value. Asserting on panic messages is brittle; the contract is "named variants are infallible, Other(_) outside 100..=999 is a programming bug."

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs (new) — comprehensive `mod method` (9 tests) + `mod status_code` (10 tests).
- jolt-core/src/lib.rs — added `#[cfg(test)] mod tests;`.
- jolt-core/src/method.rs — removed the inline `#[cfg(test)] mod tests {…}` block (2 tests, both subsumed by the new module).
- jolt-core/src/status.rs — removed the inline `#[cfg(test)] mod tests {…}` block (5 tests, all subsumed).

- phase01-method-statuscode is now CLOSED. All 4 items (007/008/009/010) are passes: true.
- JOLT-RS-011 opens phase02-request-type: Request struct with method (Method), path (String), headers (HeaderMap), query_params (HashMap<String, String>), body (Vec<u8>), cookies (Vec<Cookie>). The verification is just "struct compiles with all fields accessible" — minimum-viable. Open question to flag for that agent: which `HeaderMap` (axum::http::HeaderMap is the obvious choice given the From<StatusCode> bridge already pulls in axum::http) and which `Cookie` type (no Cookie type exists in the workspace yet — JOLT-RS-014 references RequestExt and cookies but doesn't say where Cookie is defined; likely 011 needs to either define a stub `pub struct Cookie { name: String, value: String }` in jolt-core or pull in the `cookie` crate).
