## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-011: Request struct

PRD item: JOLT-RS-011 (priority 11, phase02-request-type) — Define Request struct with method (Method), path (String), headers (HeaderMap), query_params (HashMap<String, String>), body (Vec<u8>), cookies (Vec<Cookie>). Opens phase02.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 20 passed (19 prior + tests::request::struct_literal_construction_reaches_every_field); compiled clean in 1.37s.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.41s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..010 — npm/Bun verification commands in the auto-prompt don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- HeaderMap = `axum::http::HeaderMap`. Axum is already a dep, the StatusCode bridge already pulls in axum::http, and downstream router code (phase04+) will need to read/write the same map axum hands us. Picking anything else (a hand-rolled HashMap, the http crate directly) would force conversions at every boundary.
- Cookie defined as a minimal stub `pub struct Cookie { pub name: String, pub value: String }` in a new `jolt-core/src/cookie.rs`. The previous progress entry (JOLT-RS-010 notes) flagged the choice between a stub and pulling the `cookie` crate. Chose the stub: the PRD verification only requires the struct to compile, no parsing/serialization is needed yet, and pulling a new dep without a real consumer pins a version we'd have to revisit. JOLT-RS-014 (Request::cookie accessor) and any future Set-Cookie work can extend or replace this — it's a 6-line type, cheap to evolve.
- All Request fields are `pub`. The PRD says "all fields accessible" and does not list a constructor in the steps (contrast with JOLT-RS-015 which does). Pub fields satisfy accessibility AND let JOLT-RS-012/013/014 tests construct Requests via struct literal without needing a builder API that hasn't been spec'd yet.
- Did NOT add a `Request::new(...)` constructor — not in the PRD scope. Per per-item discipline, defer until a PRD item requests it.
- Did NOT derive Default for Request. Method has no obvious default (HTTP doesn't define one), and forcing a Default impl would either require picking arbitrarily (Get?) or implementing Default for Method too. JOLT-RS-012/013/014 will likely want test helpers; those can live alongside the tests rather than in the public API.
- Re-exported Cookie + Request at the crate root via `pub use cookie::Cookie; pub use request::Request;` — same ergonomic pattern as Method and StatusCode.
- Test placed in `tests::request` submodule per the established convention (tests.rs with per-feature submodules, no inline `#[cfg(test)] mod tests` blocks alongside the source). One test that struct-literal-constructs a Request and reads each field — if any field disappears or loses pub, the test stops compiling, which IS the verification.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/cookie.rs (new) — Cookie stub struct.
- jolt-core/src/request.rs (new) — Request struct with 6 pub fields.
- jolt-core/src/lib.rs — added `pub mod cookie; pub mod request;` and `pub use cookie::Cookie; pub use request::Request;`.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added `mod request` with one accessibility test.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-011 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-012 (priority 12): `Request::header(name: &str) -> Option<&str>`. Verification names a case-insensitive lookup ("X-Test" stored, "x-test" queried returns Some). axum::http::HeaderMap already does case-insensitive lookup natively via HeaderName, so the impl is essentially `self.headers.get(name).and_then(|v| v.to_str().ok())`. Watch out: `to_str()` only succeeds for visible-ASCII values; non-ASCII bytes return Err. That's fine for typical headers; document the boundary if it matters later.
- JOLT-RS-013 (priority 13): `Request::query(key) -> Option<&str>` is trivial (`self.query_params.get(key).map(String::as_str)`); `Request::json::<T>() -> Result<T>` needs a return error type — likely a thin wrapper around serde_json::Error, or a fresh `RequestError` enum. Flag this as a small architectural choice for that agent: introducing a crate-level error type now (vs. ad-hoc per-method errors) shapes JOLT-RS-014 (`has_finished` likely doesn't fail) and the future handler trait.
- JOLT-RS-014 (priority 14): `Request::cookie(key) -> Option<&Cookie>` is straightforward. `Request::has_finished() -> bool` reads a `RequestExt` flag — but no RequestExt type exists in the workspace yet. The agent will need to either define a minimal RequestExt struct (likely an Extensions-style typed map keyed by TypeId) or stash the flag directly on Request. The PRD wording ("reads RequestExt flag") implies the former; flag this as a decision point. If RequestExt becomes a real type, it's likely also where future middleware-attached state (auth user, request-id, etc.) lives — meriting its own module.
- Cookie type is intentionally minimal. When parsing/serialization is needed, the `cookie` crate (https://crates.io/crates/cookie) or a hand-rolled parser are the two options; defer until a real consumer (Set-Cookie response header, cookie-based session middleware) appears.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-012: Request::header(name) accessor

PRD item: JOLT-RS-012 (priority 12, phase02-request-type) — Implement Request::header(name: &str) → Option<&str> with case-insensitive lookup.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 23 passed (20 prior + tests::request::header_lookup_is_case_insensitive, tests::request::header_returns_none_for_missing_name, tests::request::header_returns_none_for_non_visible_ascii_value); compiled clean in 1.09s.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.35s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..011 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace. cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Implementation is one line: `self.headers.get(name).and_then(|v| v.to_str().ok())`. axum::http::HeaderMap::get accepts `&str` (via the AsHeaderName impl that constructs a HeaderName, which lower-cases the input on the way in), so case-insensitive lookup falls out of the underlying type — no manual normalization required. Extra abstractions would just hide what the HeaderMap already does.
- Return type is `Option<&str>`, not `Option<&HeaderValue>` or `Result<Option<&str>, _>`. The PRD spec says `Option<&str>`, and `HeaderValue::to_str()` only succeeds for visible-ASCII values (HTTP !..=~ plus space/tab). For binary header values (rare in practice — non-ASCII bytes only show up in things like custom protocol extensions or malformed proxies) `to_str` returns Err, which we collapse to None. This matches the principle "if you can't render it as &str, the caller asking for &str should treat it as absent." Documented the boundary in a one-line doc comment so a future reader doesn't read the elision as "&str-coerce always succeeds."
- Added two negative tests beyond the PRD verification: missing-name returns None (locks in the basic absence path), and binary-value returns None (locks in the to_str() fallback). These are not scope creep — they are the only two ways `header()` can return None, and without them the function's contract isn't fully test-pinned. Total cost: ~10 lines of test for two behaviors that would otherwise be implicit.
- Refactored the request test module to use a `fn empty_request() -> Request` helper. Three new tests all needed a baseline Request and the existing `struct_literal_construction_reaches_every_field` test verifies struct-literal construction independently — extracting a helper for the rest avoids 30 lines of repeated boilerplate. Helper lives in the test module only; not part of the public API. If JOLT-RS-013/014 want it too, it's available.
- Did NOT add a `headers_mut()` accessor or expose any other HeaderMap-shaped API. The Request struct's `headers` field is already pub (per JOLT-RS-011's decision), so callers can mutate the underlying map directly. Adding wrapper methods now would be premature.
- Did NOT bring in the `http` crate's `AsHeaderName` trait or any generic-name overloads. The PRD signature is `header(name: &str)`, period.
- Removed the JOLT-RS-011 doc comment in request.rs that read "Field-only definition for JOLT-RS-011. Accessors (header, query, json, cookie, has_finished) land in JOLT-RS-012..014." That comment was useful as a forward-pointer when 011 was the latest item; now that 012 has landed and the `header` accessor is here, the comment is half-obsolete and would rot further as 013/014 land. Per CLAUDE-style guidance: don't reference the current task / future fixes in source comments — they belong in commit messages and progress logs.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/request.rs — added `impl Request { pub fn header(...) }` + one-line doc; trimmed the now-obsolete forward-pointer comment.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added `empty_request()` helper, 3 new tests in `tests::request` (case-insensitive lookup, missing name, binary value).
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-012 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-013 (priority 13): two methods — `Request::query(key) -> Option<&str>` and `Request::json::<T: DeserializeOwned>() -> Result<T>`. The query() side is trivial (`self.query_params.get(key).map(String::as_str)`). The json() side has a real architectural decision: what's the error type? Options: (a) return `serde_json::Result<T>` and let the caller deal with it directly — minimal but leaks the impl; (b) introduce a crate-level `RequestError` enum (possibly with thiserror) — sets up future failure modes (bad JSON, missing body, content-type mismatch) but adds scope; (c) `Result<T, serde_json::Error>` as a typed alias — middle-ground. Recommend (a) for the smallest possible step, then introducing a richer error type when JOLT-RS-016/handler trait actually needs to surface multiple failure modes. Whatever the choice, it shapes what `Result<T>` means across the API surface for the rest of phase02+.
- JOLT-RS-014 still has the open RequestExt question: where does has_finished() read from? The "RequestExt flag" in the PRD points to JOLT-RS-019's RequestExt struct, which doesn't exist yet. Two paths: (i) define a stub RequestExt now and have has_finished read it via Request.headers.extensions / a typed map, or (ii) stash the flag directly on Request as `pub finished: bool` and migrate later. Path (i) matches the PRD wording but bridges into phase04 ahead of schedule; path (ii) is simpler but means JOLT-RS-019 will need to refactor the field out. Defer the call to whoever takes 014.
- HeaderMap pattern (case-insensitive get + to_str().ok()) is now established in jolt-core. If future code (response headers, middleware) needs the same lookup, factor a free function rather than re-typing the and_then(to_str) chain.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-013: Request::query and Request::json

PRD item: JOLT-RS-013 (priority 13, phase02-request-type) — Implement Request::query(key: &str) -> Option<&str> and Request::json::<T: DeserializeOwned>() -> Result<T>.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 29 passed (23 prior + 6 new in tests::request: query_returns_value_for_present_key, query_returns_none_for_missing_key, query_lookup_is_case_sensitive, json_deserializes_body_into_struct, json_returns_err_for_malformed_body, json_returns_err_for_empty_body); compiled clean in 1.27s.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.32s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..012 — auto-prompt's npm/Bun-Hono commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- query(): one-liner `self.query_params.get(key).map(String::as_str)`. Exact-match lookup against the HashMap<String, String> field — no case folding, no URL-decoding (the field already holds decoded values per the JOLT-RS-011 contract). HashMap::get is exact-string lookup, so callers passing a different case get None; locked that in with `query_lookup_is_case_sensitive`.
- json(): returns `serde_json::Result<T>` directly per the option-(a) recommendation flagged in the JOLT-RS-012 progress notes. Smallest-possible step: no crate-level RequestError enum yet, no thiserror dep, no Result type alias. When JOLT-RS-016+ need to surface multiple failure modes (bad JSON, missing body, content-type mismatch, etc.) via a unified error, a single migration touches every json() call site at once — cheaper than introducing a thin alias now and refactoring twice.
- Implementation uses `serde_json::from_slice(&self.body)` rather than `from_str(std::str::from_utf8(...)?)`. from_slice is the canonical entrypoint for deserializing raw bytes (it handles UTF-8 validation as part of parsing) and avoids an extra allocation/error path. Empty bodies and non-JSON payloads naturally surface as serde_json::Error — verified by `json_returns_err_for_empty_body` and `json_returns_err_for_malformed_body`.
- Bound is `T: DeserializeOwned` exactly per the PRD spec. DeserializeOwned (= for<'de> Deserialize<'de>) is required because the body bytes are owned by &self and the deserialized value must outlive the call — no zero-copy borrows. If/when a future PRD item wants borrowed deserialization (e.g. &str fields pointing into the body), that'd be a separate `json_borrowed` method, not a generic-relaxation of this one.
- Added `use serde::de::DeserializeOwned;` at the top of request.rs. serde is already a direct dep of jolt-core (workspace pin includes derive feature); the import is the one new line of crate-graph surface.
- Test struct `Item { name: String, count: u32 }` is defined inside the test fn rather than at module scope — it's needed only by one test, and a module-scoped helper struct would invite unrelated tests to share it and accidentally couple their expectations.
- The "malformed body" and "empty body" tests both deserialize into `serde_json::Value` rather than a strongly-typed struct. Value accepts any valid JSON, so the test pinpoints "not valid JSON" as the failure cause rather than "valid JSON but wrong shape" — keeps the test honest about what's actually being asserted.
- Did NOT add a `query_iter()` or `queries(key)` method for repeated keys (e.g. `?tag=a&tag=b`). The query_params field is `HashMap<String, String>` (one-value-per-key) per JOLT-RS-011, so multi-value queries collapse on insert. If multi-value support becomes needed, the right move is to widen the field type (HashMap<String, Vec<String>> or a multimap), not to layer methods over a single-value map. Out of scope for this PRD item.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/request.rs — added `use serde::de::DeserializeOwned;`, `Request::query`, `Request::json`.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added 6 tests in `tests::request` (3 for query, 3 for json).
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-013 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-014 (priority 14, closes phase02): Request::cookie(key) -> Option<&Cookie> and Request::has_finished() -> bool. cookie() is straightforward (linear scan over self.cookies returning the first matching name, since Cookie is currently a 2-field stub and there's no map index). has_finished() still has the open RequestExt question flagged in JOLT-RS-012 notes: option (i) define a stub RequestExt now and read it via axum::http::Extensions; option (ii) stash the flag directly on Request as `pub finished: bool` and migrate later. Recommend (ii) for the smallest step — JOLT-RS-019 explicitly creates RequestExt with AtomicBool, and JOLT-RS-021 wires it through Extensions; prematurely shoehorning RequestExt into Request now bridges into phase04 ahead of schedule. Revisit when 019/021 arrive.
- After 014, phase02 closes and phase03 begins (JOLT-RS-015: Response<T> struct with status, headers, body + new() constructor). That's the first generic type in the codebase — flag the Serialize bound choice (struct-level vs. impl-block) for that agent.
- json() error surface deliberately leaks `serde_json::Error`. If a JOLT-RS-016+ item wants to wrap this in a Jolt-specific RequestError (e.g. for unified handler error-to-status mapping), the migration is mechanical: change the return type and update each call site. No callers exist outside the test module yet.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-014: Request::cookie and Request::has_finished

PRD item: JOLT-RS-014 (priority 14, phase02-request-type) — Implement Request::cookie(key: &str) -> Option<&Cookie> and Request::has_finished() -> bool. Closes phase02.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 35 passed (29 prior + 6 new in tests::request: cookie_returns_matching_entry, cookie_returns_none_for_missing_name, cookie_lookup_is_case_sensitive, cookie_returns_first_match_when_duplicate_names_exist, has_finished_defaults_to_false, has_finished_reflects_finished_flag); compiled clean.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.37s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..013 — auto-prompt's npm/Bun-Hono commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- has_finished() reads a new `pub finished: bool` field on Request — option (ii) from the JOLT-RS-013 progress notes. Picked this over defining a stub RequestExt now because: (a) JOLT-RS-019 explicitly creates RequestExt with AtomicBool — defining a stub here just to be replaced 5 items later is churn; (b) JOLT-RS-021 wires RequestExt through axum::http::Extensions, which Request doesn't currently expose — bridging that surface ahead of schedule means inventing an extensions field whose shape is still under-specified; (c) the migration from `pub finished: bool` to `RequestExt::is_finished()` looked up from Extensions is mechanical: one field removed, has_finished()'s body changes. Test setup in 014 just sets `req.finished = true`, which is symmetric to how 020/021 will use `req.extensions().get::<RequestExt>()?.mark_finished()` later.
- cookie() is a linear scan via `self.cookies.iter().find(|c| c.name == name)`. cookies is `Vec<Cookie>` per JOLT-RS-011 — no map index, so linear is the natural shape. Returns the first match when duplicates exist (locked in by `cookie_returns_first_match_when_duplicate_names_exist`); the alternative (last match, or all matches) would be a bigger API decision and isn't requested here. If cookie lookups become a hot path or duplicate-name handling needs to differ, the right move is to widen the underlying field type, not to layer a different lookup over the same Vec.
- cookie() name match is case-sensitive per RFC 6265 §4.1.2 (cookie names are case-sensitive on the wire). Locked in by `cookie_lookup_is_case_sensitive`. This contrasts with header() which is case-insensitive (RFC 9110 §5.1) — different RFCs, different rules.
- cookie() returns `Option<&Cookie>` per the PRD spec. Returning the whole Cookie (currently a 2-field name/value stub) instead of just &str-of-value lets callers read both name and value; `&Cookie` keeps the borrow tied to self with no allocation.
- Updated `empty_request()` test helper and the existing `struct_literal_construction_reaches_every_field` test to set `finished: false`. Added an assertion for the new field in the struct-literal test so dropping the field would fail compilation AND assertion. No other test changes needed — all prior tests continue to pass via the helper.
- Added 4 cookie tests + 2 has_finished tests. PRD verification only requires "cookie extraction and finished-flag reading work" — covered by cookie_returns_matching_entry + has_finished_reflects_finished_flag. Negative paths (missing name, case-sensitivity, duplicate-name first-match, default-false) lock in the contract so a future refactor can't silently change behavior. Total ~50 lines of test code for behaviors that would otherwise be implicit.
- Did NOT add a `cookies(name)` (plural) accessor returning all matching cookies, nor a `cookies_iter()`. self.cookies is already pub, so callers needing those can iterate the field directly. Wrapper methods would be premature.
- Did NOT migrate any test to a setter method like `mark_finished()`. JOLT-RS-020 owns that method (on RequestExt). For now, mutating `req.finished` directly is the simplest path; it'll change call sites once 020/021 land.
- Did NOT touch the public re-exports in lib.rs. Cookie + Request were re-exported in JOLT-RS-011; the new accessors don't introduce new types.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/request.rs — added `pub finished: bool` field + `cookie()` and `has_finished()` methods.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — extended `empty_request()` helper, updated struct-literal test, added 6 new tests.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-014 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- phase02-request-type is now CLOSED. All 4 items (011/012/013/014) are passes: true.
- JOLT-RS-015 opens phase03-response-type: `Response<T: Serialize>` struct with status (StatusCode), headers (HeaderMap), body (T) + Response::new(status, body) constructor. First generic type in the codebase. Architectural question to flag for that agent: where does the Serialize bound go — on the struct definition itself (`pub struct Response<T: Serialize>`) or only on the impl blocks that need it (`impl<T: Serialize> Response<T>`)? Convention in idiomatic Rust is the latter — keep struct definitions free of bounds, attach them to the impls that actually need them. This lets `Response<()>` or `Response<Vec<u8>>` types work in contexts that don't serialize, and is the same pattern serde uses. The PRD step says "Response<T: Serialize>" but that's just shorthand; idiomatic Rust will move it to impls. The PRD verification ("Compiles, new() constructs valid Response") doesn't pin this either way.
- When JOLT-RS-019/020/021 land, the migration plan for the `finished` flag: (1) JOLT-RS-019 defines RequestExt { finished: AtomicBool }; (2) JOLT-RS-020 adds mark_finished()/is_finished(); (3) JOLT-RS-021 either adds an `extensions: axum::http::Extensions` field to Request (storing RequestExt there), or removes the `finished` field entirely if Request gets wrapped by an axum-Request-aware shim. The has_finished() body becomes `self.extensions.get::<RequestExt>().is_some_and(|ext| ext.is_finished())` (or whatever shape 021 settles on). The current `pub finished: bool` field gets deleted. cookie() does not need to change.
- Cookie type remains the 2-field stub (name + value). When parsing/serialization is needed, defer to either the `cookie` crate or hand-rolled — same call as flagged in JOLT-RS-011 notes.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-015: Response<T> struct + new() constructor

PRD item: JOLT-RS-015 (priority 15, phase03-response-type) — Define Response<T: Serialize> struct with status (StatusCode), headers (HeaderMap), body (T) and a Response::new(status, body) constructor. Opens phase03.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 37 passed (35 prior + tests::response::new_constructs_response_with_given_status_and_body, tests::response::struct_literal_construction_reaches_every_field); 0 failed.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.38s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..014 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Struct definition has NO trait bounds: `pub struct Response<T> { ... }` rather than `Response<T: Serialize>`. Per the JOLT-RS-014 progress notes' architectural flag and idiomatic Rust convention (mirrors serde itself), bounds belong on impl blocks that need them — not on the struct. This lets `Response<()>`, `Response<Vec<u8>>`, and other non-serialize bodies work in contexts that don't need JSON encoding (e.g. NoContent responses, raw byte streaming, future Response<String> for text/plain in JOLT-RS-017). The PRD's "T: Serialize" wording is shorthand; the bound only matters when JOLT-RS-016 actually serializes the body.
- new() takes (status, body) and initializes headers to an empty HeaderMap. Callers add headers post-construction via the pub headers field (or via builder methods that future PRD items may add). This matches the PRD's exact two-arg signature and avoids inventing a fluent API ahead of need.
- All three fields are `pub`. Same rationale as Request (JOLT-RS-011): the PRD doesn't gate access through methods, and pub fields let JOLT-RS-016/017/018 build Responses via struct literals without needing a builder API that hasn't been spec'd. Most consumers will use new() + field-mutation.
- Did NOT derive Default. T has no obvious default in the general case, and adding `where T: Default` to the derive would silently restrict the API. If a Response<()> default is wanted, JOLT-RS-018 can decide.
- Did NOT add response.headers_mut() or any builder methods (with_header, with_status, etc.). Out of scope for JOLT-RS-015. The pub headers field gives raw access; future PRD items can layer ergonomics if needed.
- Module file is `src/response.rs` (mirrors `request.rs`'s short name). Re-exported at the crate root via `pub use response::Response;` — same ergonomic pattern as Request, Method, StatusCode, Cookie.
- Two tests in tests::response submodule: (1) new() with a u32 body verifies status + body + empty headers; (2) struct-literal construction with a `()` body verifies every field is reachable AND that the struct compiles for non-serialize body types — locking in the no-bound-on-struct decision so a future regression that adds `T: Serialize` to the struct definition would fail this test (since `()` is Serialize, the test still wouldn't catch it directly, but it documents intent and exercises an unusual body shape). Could be tightened with a `#[derive(Default)] struct NoSerial;` body to test against any future `T: Serialize` regression on the struct itself; deferred as scope creep.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/response.rs (new) — Response<T> struct with 3 pub fields + new(status, body) constructor.
- jolt-core/src/lib.rs — added `pub mod response;` and `pub use response::Response;`.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added `mod response` with 2 tests.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-015 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-016 (priority 16): `impl<T: Serialize> Into<axum::response::Response> for Response<T>`. Bounds go on the impl, not the struct (already locked in by 015). Implementation: serialize body via `serde_json::to_vec(&self.body)` (handle the Result — what status to return on serialize failure? likely `StatusCode::InternalServerError` with an empty body, or panic with an explicit expect since types that opt into Response<T: Serialize> should have infallible serialization in practice). Set Content-Type: application/json header. Set status via `axum::http::StatusCode::from(self.status)`. Need to merge self.headers into the response builder — axum::response::Response::builder().status(...).header(...).body(...) is the natural shape; iterate self.headers to forward each one. Watch out: the Into impl will conflict with JOLT-RS-017's Into impls for Response<String> and Response<&str> unless 017 uses specialization (unstable) or the impls are on concrete types only. If 017 uses `impl Into<...> for Response<String>` specifically (no generics), it conflicts with the blanket `impl<T: Serialize> Into<...> for Response<T>` because String IS Serialize. Real fix: 017 needs to use a different mechanism — perhaps a marker trait (TextResponseBody?) or distinct method names (into_text_response()) — OR 016's blanket impl needs a narrower bound (e.g. a custom `JsonBody` marker trait that String/str don't impl). Flag this conflict prominently for whoever takes 016 and 017 together; it's an architectural decision that may require revisiting both.
- JOLT-RS-017 (priority 17): hinges on the resolution above. Two viable paths: (a) make 016 narrow (e.g. only Response<serde_json::Value>, or only Response<T> where T: Serialize + JsonBody marker), then 017 adds plain Response<String> / Response<&str> impls without conflict; (b) keep 016 as a generic blanket and have 017 use a wrapper type like `Response<Text>` where Text wraps String. Path (a) is more idiomatic; path (b) avoids re-touching 016. Recommend (a) — introduce a sealed `JsonBody` (or similar) trait in 016 with a blanket `impl<T: Serialize> JsonBody for T` IF that doesn't break the orphan rules + leaves 017 free. But the simpler fix may be: define `Response<T>::into_axum_json(self)` and `Response<String>::into_axum_text(self)` as inherent methods rather than From/Into impls — sidestepping coherence entirely. JOLT-RS-016 uses the word "Into" explicitly though, so deferring to From/Into may be required by the PRD wording.
- JOLT-RS-018 (priority 18, closes phase03): comprehensive tests across json/string/empty body types. Same shape as JOLT-RS-010's tests::status_code submodule — table-driven where possible, asserts on body bytes + content-type header + status.
- After 018, phase04 begins (JOLT-RS-019: RequestExt with AtomicBool). The migration of `Request.finished` field (currently `pub finished: bool`) to `RequestExt::is_finished()` lookup happens in JOLT-RS-021 per the JOLT-RS-014 progress notes.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-016: Response<T: Serialize> → axum::response::Response

PRD item: JOLT-RS-016 (priority 16, phase03-response-type) — Implement Into<axum::response::Response> for Response<T> where T: Serialize: serialize body as JSON, set content-type: application/json, set status.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 39 passed (37 prior + 2 new in tests::response: into_axum_response_serializes_json_with_content_type_and_status, into_axum_response_forwards_custom_headers); compiled clean in 1.63s.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.43s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..015 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Implemented `From<Response<T>> for axum::response::Response` rather than `Into` directly. The blanket `impl<T, U> Into<U> for T where U: From<T>` gives Into for free, and the test (`.into()`) exercises that path. Idiomatic Rust convention; the PRD's "Implement Into<...>" wording is satisfied at the call site.
- Bound (`T: Serialize`) lives on the impl block, not the struct definition — locked in by JOLT-RS-015's "no bounds on struct" decision. `Response<()>`, `Response<Vec<u8>>`, etc. continue to be valid types; only the From impl requires Serialize.
- Body serialized via `serde_json::to_vec(&body)` (canonical bytes-out path) wrapped in `axum::body::Body::from(...)`. Errors are `.expect(...)` rather than handled — the contract is "T: Serialize means infallible JSON for sane types." Custom Serialize impls that intentionally fail (e.g. via Serializer error reporting) are a programming bug, not a recoverable runtime condition; same philosophy as the StatusCode → axum bridge in JOLT-RS-009.
- Custom headers are forwarded via `response.headers_mut().extend(headers)` (consumes the source HeaderMap), then `Content-Type: application/json` is inserted last so it OVERRIDES any caller-set Content-Type. The PRD says "set content-type: application/json" unambiguously — for non-JSON content-types, callers should use a different conversion path (JOLT-RS-017 covers text/plain). Used `extend` (not loop+insert) because HeaderMap supports multi-value headers and `extend` handles the (Option<HeaderName>, HeaderValue) iterator shape correctly; a naive insert loop would silently collapse multi-value headers.
- Tests use `#[tokio::test]` since `axum::body::to_bytes` is async. tokio is already a direct dep with `features = ["full"]` per the workspace pin, which includes the `macros` feature that powers `#[tokio::test]`. No new deps; no per-crate feature flags. `axum::body::to_bytes(body, 1024)` size cap is 1KB — generous for the 17-byte JSON test payload, tight enough that an unbounded body bug would surface immediately.
- Added a second test (`into_axum_response_forwards_custom_headers`) beyond the PRD's single verification line. PRD verification names "correct JSON body and headers" but only one test is hard to read as proving header-forwarding works (the empty-headers case is degenerate). Adding a custom-header test pins the `extend` behavior so a future regression that drops/clobbers headers would fail loudly. Total cost: ~20 lines of test for a load-bearing invariant.
- Did NOT add tests for Other(599) status passthrough or for non-Object JSON bodies (numbers, arrays, strings) — JOLT-RS-018 is explicitly the "comprehensive tests across body types" item, and pre-empting its scope would force JOLT-RS-018 to either skip those or duplicate. Stay in lane.
- ⚠️ KNOWN UPCOMING CONFLICT: This blanket `impl<T: Serialize> From<Response<T>> for axum::response::Response` will COLLIDE with JOLT-RS-017's `impl From<Response<String>> for axum::response::Response` (and `Response<&str>`) because String/&str both implement Serialize. The conflict was flagged in JOLT-RS-015's progress notes and remains the next agent's architectural call. Two viable resolutions: (a) introduce a sealed `JsonBody` marker trait in this file with a blanket `impl<T: Serialize> JsonBody for T` exception list excluding String/&str (impossible — sealed traits don't support negative impls), so realistically: define `JsonBody` as a manually-implemented sealed marker with explicit impls for Value, &Value, primitives, and any struct that should round-trip as JSON; OR (b) wrap String in a `Text<String>` newtype and have `Response<Text<String>>` route to text/plain. Path (a) is more invasive but more idiomatic. JOLT-RS-017's agent will need to refactor THIS impl — accept that and don't try to anticipate the marker trait now (would be over-engineering for an item the PRD doesn't yet ask for). The current implementation is exactly what JOLT-RS-016 specifies.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/response.rs — added `use axum::body::Body;`, `use axum::http::header::CONTENT_TYPE;`, `use axum::http::HeaderValue;`, `use serde::Serialize;`; added `impl<T: Serialize> From<Response<T>> for axum::response::Response`.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added 2 `#[tokio::test]` cases in `tests::response`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-016 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-017 (priority 17): the impl conflict above is the central problem. Recommended approach: refactor JOLT-RS-016's impl to use a sealed marker trait (e.g. `pub trait JsonBody: Serialize {}` with explicit impls per-type), then add Response<String>/Response<&str> impls without overlap. This is a JOLT-RS-016 refactor disguised as JOLT-RS-017 work — be honest about it in that progress entry. Alternative: scrap the blanket and require callers to pick a method (`.into_json_response()` vs `.into_text_response()`), but that violates the PRD's "Into" wording.
- JOLT-RS-018 (closes phase03): comprehensive tests across body types (json/string/empty/NoContent). Will need updated test surface depending on how 017 resolves the conflict. Suggested coverage once 017 lands: each named StatusCode → correct axum status; JSON body bytes match expected serialization for u32/Vec/struct; String/&str body bytes match expected raw text; NoContent (204) produces an empty body or correctly-sized empty body; custom headers forward; Content-Type is set per body family (application/json vs text/plain).
- The Content-Type override behavior (framework-set, not caller-overridable) is now load-bearing for the JSON path. If a future feature wants to support custom JSON Content-Types (e.g. application/vnd.api+json), it'll need a deliberate API decision — not a silent caller-side override.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-017: Response<String> / Response<&str> → text/plain

PRD item: JOLT-RS-017 (priority 17, phase03-response-type) — Implement Into<axum::response::Response> for Response<String> and Response<&str> with content-type: text/plain.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 42 passed (39 prior + 3 new in tests::response: into_axum_response_with_string_body_uses_text_plain, into_axum_response_with_str_body_uses_text_plain, into_axum_response_with_string_body_forwards_custom_headers); 0 failed.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.34s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..016 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Resolved the trait coherence conflict flagged in JOLT-RS-016 progress notes by introducing an OPEN marker trait `pub trait JsonBody: Serialize {}` (NOT sealed). The blanket From impl is now `impl<T: JsonBody> From<Response<T>> for axum::response::Response` instead of `impl<T: Serialize> ...`. String and &str do NOT implement JsonBody, so the new concrete `impl From<Response<String>>` and `impl<'a> From<Response<&'a str>>` impls coexist with the JSON blanket without overlap. Compiler accepts this because: (a) String/&str aren't currently JsonBody-impl'd in jolt-core, (b) downstream crates can't add `impl JsonBody for String` due to orphan rules (both foreign to them), (c) future jolt-core additions adding such an impl would fail compile-time coherence at that moment, not now.
- Picked OPEN over SEALED trait. Sealed (per JOLT-RS-016 notes' suggestion) would force users to wrap their own structs (e.g. via a future derive macro) before using them as JSON bodies. Open lets handler authors write `impl JsonBody for MyStruct {}` (one trivial line) alongside their `Serialize` derive. The sealed-vs-open trade-off: sealed is more explicit/controllable, open is more ergonomic. Chose open because the framework's UX target is "write a struct, derive Serialize, return Response<MyStruct>" — gating that behind a derive macro the framework doesn't have yet would block JSON handlers indefinitely.
- Provided JsonBody impls for: (), bool, i8/i16/i32/i64, u8/u16/u32/u64, f32, f64, serde_json::Value. Notable omissions: String, &str (intentional — they route to text/plain). Also omitted: Vec<T>, Option<T>, HashMap<String, T>, structs. JOLT-RS-018's "comprehensive tests" item will reveal what additional impls are needed; defer adding them until tests demand them. Adding speculative impls now is over-engineering.
- &str impl uses `impl<'a> From<Response<&'a str>>` (any lifetime), not `impl From<Response<&'static str>>`. Implementation copies via `.to_string()` to get an owned body. The 'static-only alternative would be marginally faster (`Bytes::from_static`) but rejects `let s: &str = &local; Response::new(Ok, s)` patterns. Cost of the copy: trivial vs. correctness/ergonomics gain.
- Both text impls use `text/plain; charset=utf-8` content-type, not bare `text/plain`. PRD says "text/plain" but utf-8 charset is the conventional default for Rust string bodies (which are UTF-8 by construction) and matches axum's own String IntoResponse behavior. A bare `text/plain` would be technically PRD-compliant but would represent a regression for downstream consumers vs. axum's idiom. If a future PRD item requires bare text/plain for some reason, easy to relax.
- Extracted `finalize_axum_response(status, headers, body, content_type)` helper to share the response-builder + header-extension + content-type-insertion sequence across the JSON, String, and &str impls. Three near-identical blocks would otherwise drift over time. Helper is `fn` (not pub) since it's internal-only. Tiny refactor of JOLT-RS-016's existing impl is included here — same control-flow, just routed through the helper. Verified by re-running the two existing JSON tests post-refactor.
- Re-exported `JsonBody` at the crate root via `pub use response::{JsonBody, Response};` — consumers will need to reference the trait when impl-ing it for their own structs. Same ergonomic precedent as Cookie/Method/Request/Response/StatusCode re-exports.
- Added 3 tests in `tests::response`: (1) Response<String> → text/plain + correct body bytes; (2) Response<&str> → text/plain + correct body bytes; (3) Response<String> forwards custom headers (mirrors the JSON header-forwarding test, locks in that the helper handles header extension uniformly). PRD verification line names only "Response<String> → text/plain"; the &str case isn't in the verification but IS in the steps ("for Response<String> and Response<&str>"), so test #2 is required to prove the impl actually works rather than merely compiles. Test #3 is a regression guard for the helper extraction.
- Did NOT add a Response<&str> custom-headers test. Same code path as Response<String> via the helper; one would-be-redundant test isn't worth the line count.
- Did NOT add Vec<u8> or octet-stream support. Out of scope; if a binary body type becomes necessary, a future PRD item would either add `impl JsonBody for Vec<u8>` (treats as JSON array of integers — probably wrong) or introduce a separate `impl From<Response<Vec<u8>>>` with `application/octet-stream`. Defer.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/response.rs — added `pub trait JsonBody: Serialize {}` + 13 leaf impls; changed JSON From impl bound from `T: Serialize` to `T: JsonBody`; added `impl From<Response<String>>` + `impl<'a> From<Response<&'a str>>` text/plain impls; extracted private `finalize_axum_response` helper.
- jolt-core/src/lib.rs — `pub use response::Response` → `pub use response::{JsonBody, Response}`.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added 3 `#[tokio::test]` cases in `tests::response`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-017 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-018 (priority 18, closes phase03): comprehensive tests across body types (json, string, empty/NoContent). Coverage to consider: each named StatusCode → correct axum status (probably already proven by JOLT-RS-010, but verify the bridging path doesn't drop the variant); JSON body bytes match expected serialization for at least one primitive (u32 already covered) + serde_json::Value (already covered); Response<()> → JSON `null` body with application/json content-type (verifies the `()` JsonBody impl); Response<String> NoContent — what's the expected behavior with a non-empty String body and a 204 status? RFC 7230 says 204 MUST have empty body; we currently send the String as-is (no enforcement). Decision: for now, don't enforce (callers responsible). 018 should test current behavior (body is sent regardless of status), with a comment that an enforcement layer could be added later. Body length cap on `axum::body::to_bytes` should be raised (currently 1024) only if a test needs a large body; default to 1024.
- JOLT-RS-018's tests will likely need additional JsonBody impls. Common ones: `impl<T: JsonBody> JsonBody for Vec<T>` and `impl<T: JsonBody> JsonBody for Option<T>` — both are standard JSON shapes. Consider also `HashMap<String, T> where T: JsonBody`. Add these in 018 when a test demands them, not preemptively.
- Phase04 begins with JOLT-RS-019 (RequestExt with AtomicBool). The deferred Request.finished migration plan in JOLT-RS-014's notes is still authoritative.
- Doc-test note: the `JsonBody` doc-comment example (`impl JsonBody for MyStruct {}`) is illustrative only, not a doc test (no ```rust block). If JOLT-RS-018 or later adds doc tests anywhere, ensure JsonBody's doc is reviewed for example correctness.
- Naming: chose `JsonBody` over alternatives like `Json`, `JsonResponse`, `IntoJson`. `Json` would conflict with the obvious axum::Json wrapper name pattern; `JsonResponse` is misleading (it's the body, not the response); `IntoJson` would suggest a method that converts. `JsonBody` reads as "this type IS a JSON body" — which matches its usage as a type-level marker.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-018: Comprehensive Response body-type tests (closes phase03)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-018 (priority 18, phase03-response-type) — Write unit tests for all Response body types (json, string, empty/NoContent). Closes phase03.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::response` → 19 passed (7 prior + 12 new), 0 failed, 35 filtered out; finished in 0.00s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 54 passed total (up from 42); 0 failed.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.21s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..017 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Added 12 new tests in `tests::response` covering the gaps flagged in JOLT-RS-016/017 progress notes:
  * `into_axum_response_with_unit_body_serializes_as_json_null` — Response<()> → "null", application/json. Locks in the () JsonBody impl's actual body bytes (previously only the impl existed; no body-bytes test).
  * `into_axum_response_with_bool_body_serializes_as_json_boolean` — both true and false in one test (combined since they share the code path; splitting would be redundant).
  * `into_axum_response_with_integer_body_serializes_as_json_number` — Response<i32> → "42" body bytes (the existing `forwards_custom_headers` test uses u32 but only asserts headers).
  * `into_axum_response_with_float_body_serializes_as_json_number` — Response<f64> → "1.5" body bytes.
  * `into_axum_response_with_json_array_value_serializes_correctly` — serde_json::Value array (existing test only covered Object).
  * `into_axum_response_with_user_defined_struct_body_serializes_as_json` — proves the OPEN JsonBody marker trait actually works for user code: `#[derive(Serialize)] struct Item; impl JsonBody for Item {}` → JSON body bytes. This is the load-bearing test for the JOLT-RS-017 architectural decision (open vs sealed marker). If a future change accidentally seals JsonBody (e.g. moves it to a private supertrait or adds a sealed marker bound), this test fails to compile.
  * `into_axum_response_with_empty_string_body_sends_empty_body` and `into_axum_response_with_empty_str_body_sends_empty_body` — empty String / empty &str → empty body bytes, text/plain. Locks in that the bridge doesn't synthesize a placeholder for empty bodies.
  * `into_axum_response_status_passes_through_named_variants` — table-driven over Ok/Created/NoContent/BadRequest/NotFound/InternalServerError. JOLT-RS-010 tested the StatusCode→axum bridge in isolation; this test proves the Response→axum bridge actually invokes that conversion (would catch e.g. a regression that hardcoded 200 in the builder).
  * `into_axum_response_status_passes_through_other_variant` — Other(418) → axum status 418. Closes the named/Other passthrough surface.
  * `into_axum_response_no_content_with_string_body_sends_body_as_is` — DOCUMENTS the deliberate non-enforcement of RFC 7230 §3.3.3 ("204 MUST have empty body"). The bridge ships the caller's body verbatim. Inline comment explicitly says "if enforcement is added later, update this test, don't delete it" — so a future agent doesn't remove the test thinking it's a bug-locking test for a bug.
  * `into_axum_response_overrides_caller_set_content_type` — caller sets Content-Type: application/xml on Response<u32>; framework overrides with application/json. Locks in the precedence rule from JOLT-RS-016 (response.headers_mut().extend then insert CONTENT_TYPE last) which the prior progress notes flagged as "load-bearing for the JSON path." Without this test, a refactor that swaps `extend` and `insert` order would silently let caller Content-Types win.
- Extracted a `body_bytes(response) -> Vec<u8>` async test helper that wraps `axum::body::to_bytes(_, 1024)` + `.unwrap()` + `.to_vec()`. The existing tests inline this 3-line dance; the 8 new tests that read body bytes use the helper. Did NOT refactor the prior tests (JOLT-RS-016/017's body-reading tests) to use the helper — they pre-date the helper, work fine, and changing them is out of JOLT-RS-018's scope (would muddy the diff). If a future PRD touches those tests, swapping in the helper is trivial.
- Did NOT add new JsonBody impls (Vec<T>, Option<T>, HashMap<String, T>, etc.) per JOLT-RS-017's flagged guidance: "Add these in 018 when a test demands them, not preemptively." None of the body-type tests require them — primitives + Value + user-defined struct are sufficient to prove the bridge handles the full JSON shape space (since serde_json::Value can represent arrays/objects/null already, and user structs prove the extension point).
- Did NOT add a test for JOLT-RS-016's "binary header value forwarding" or any header-edge-case beyond the existing trace-id tests. Those belong with the header surface, not the body-type surface; out of scope for 018's "body types" framing.
- Test naming follows the existing `into_axum_response_with_<body>_<assertion>` pattern. The `_status_passes_through_*` and `_overrides_caller_set_content_type` tests deviate from that pattern intentionally — they're cross-cutting (any body type) rather than body-specific.
- All new tests use `#[tokio::test]` (axum::body::to_bytes is async) — consistent with JOLT-RS-016/017's tests. tokio is already a workspace dep with `features = ["full"]`.
- Test `body_bytes` helper has the 1024-byte cap from prior tests. None of the new tests need bigger bodies (the largest is 27 bytes for the user-struct JSON). If a future test needs to push more, raise it locally rather than globally — keeps unbounded-body bugs surfacing fast.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added `body_bytes` async helper and 12 new `#[tokio::test]` cases in `tests::response`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-018 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- phase03-response-type is now CLOSED. All 4 items (015/016/017/018) are passes: true.
- JOLT-RS-019 opens phase04-requestext-flag: `RequestExt struct with finished: AtomicBool. Implement new() defaulting to false.` First atomic primitive in the codebase. Architectural questions for that agent:
  * `AtomicBool` requires `std::sync::atomic::AtomicBool` and an Ordering choice for load/store. Defer the Ordering question to JOLT-RS-020 (which adds mark_finished/is_finished); 019 is just struct definition + new(). Likely Ordering::Relaxed for both — finished is a one-way latch (false → true), no other state hangs off it, no acquire/release relationship to another datum.
  * Where does RequestExt live in the module tree? Two viable options: (a) new `jolt-core/src/request_ext.rs` module, mirroring `request.rs` and `response.rs`; (b) submodule of `request` (extend `request.rs` or add `request/ext.rs`). Recommend (a) — RequestExt is conceptually a different type of state (mutable, async-shared) than Request (immutable, owned), and a flat module list at the crate root is the established pattern. Re-export at crate root via `pub use request_ext::RequestExt` per the precedent of Cookie/Method/Request/Response/StatusCode.
  * AtomicBool is `!Default` if a non-zero default is needed, but defaults to `false` via `AtomicBool::new(false)`. The PRD says "defaults to false" so `new()` is `Self { finished: AtomicBool::new(false) }`. If `Default` derive is wanted, `#[derive(Default)]` works (AtomicBool::default() == AtomicBool::new(false)) — but only do this if a downstream consumer asks; otherwise overspecified.
- JOLT-RS-021 (priority 21): the deferred `Request.finished` field migration. Per JOLT-RS-014 progress notes: the migration plan is mechanical — JOLT-RS-021 either adds an `extensions: axum::http::Extensions` field to Request and stores RequestExt there, or wraps Request in a shim type. The current `pub finished: bool` field on Request gets deleted at that point. `has_finished()` body switches from `self.finished` to whatever lookup 021 settles on. The JOLT-RS-014 `has_finished_reflects_finished_flag` test will need to be rewritten to use `mark_finished()` (from JOLT-RS-020) instead of `req.finished = true`.
- JsonBody trait is openness now locked in by `into_axum_response_with_user_defined_struct_body_serializes_as_json`. Future agents wanting to seal the trait must explicitly delete or rework that test — not a silent refactor.
- Content-Type override precedence for the JSON path is locked in. A symmetric test for the text/plain path (`Response<String>` with caller-set CONTENT_TYPE) was NOT added — same code path through `finalize_axum_response`, would be redundant. If the helper is ever broken into per-content-type branches, add the symmetric test then.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-019: RequestExt struct with finished AtomicBool (opens phase04)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-019 (priority 19, phase04-requestext-flag) — Define RequestExt struct with finished: AtomicBool. Implement new() defaulting to false.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-core` → clean in 0.80s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::request_ext` → 2/2 passed (54 filtered out); 0 failed.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.30s; no regressions.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 56 passed total (up from 54); 0 failed.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..018 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Placed `RequestExt` at `jolt-core/src/request_ext.rs` per JOLT-RS-018 progress note recommendation: flat module list at crate root mirrors `request.rs` / `response.rs` precedent. The alternative (submodule of `request`) would conflate two conceptually distinct types — Request (immutable owned snapshot) vs RequestExt (mutable async-shared state).
- Re-exported as `pub use request_ext::RequestExt` in `lib.rs` matching the precedent for Cookie/Method/Request/Response/StatusCode.
- Field is `pub finished: AtomicBool` (consistent with Request's all-pub-fields pattern). Direct field access lets tests verify the default without committing to an Ordering choice or a `is_finished()` API — both of those belong to JOLT-RS-020.
- `#[derive(Debug)]` only — NOT Clone (AtomicBool is `!Clone` because cloning interior mutability is ambiguous; per-field clone via `.load()` would silently break the shared-state semantics that motivate the type). NOT `Default` either — JOLT-RS-018's notes explicitly flagged Default as "only do this if a downstream consumer asks; otherwise overspecified," and the PRD says `new()` not `default()`.
- `new()` uses `AtomicBool::new(false)` rather than `AtomicBool::default()` — they're equivalent (`AtomicBool::default() == AtomicBool::new(false)`), but `new(false)` reads as the intent stated in the PRD ("defaulting to false") without relying on a Default impl that we deliberately don't derive.
- Did NOT add `mark_finished()` / `is_finished()` methods — those are JOLT-RS-020. The Ordering question is therefore deferred (the test reads `finished` directly with `Ordering::Relaxed`, but that's a test-local choice, not an API choice).
- Did NOT integrate RequestExt with Request yet — that's JOLT-RS-021 (axum Extensions registration) and follows the deferred Request.finished migration flagged in JOLT-RS-014's notes.

Tests added (2 in `tests::request_ext`):
- `new_constructs_with_finished_defaulting_to_false` — `RequestExt::new()` then `finished.load(Ordering::Relaxed)` is false. Tests the construction path.
- `new_into_inner_reports_false` — `RequestExt::new()` then `finished.into_inner()` is false. The comment explicitly notes this is independent of any Ordering API choice the load path picks; protects against a 020 refactor that changes Ordering and accidentally breaks default semantics.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/request_ext.rs — new file: `pub struct RequestExt { pub finished: AtomicBool }` + `pub fn new() -> Self`.
- jolt-core/src/lib.rs — added `pub mod request_ext;` and `pub use request_ext::RequestExt;`.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added `mod request_ext` with 2 unit tests.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-019 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-020 (priority 20): adds `mark_finished()` and `is_finished()`. Ordering recommendation: `Ordering::Relaxed` for both — `finished` is a one-way latch (false → true), no other state hangs off it, no acquire/release relationship to another datum. If a future requirement adds state that must be visible alongside the flip (e.g. a "finished_by" middleware-id field), upgrade to Release/Acquire then. The methods take `&self` (not `&mut self`) — that's the whole point of using AtomicBool over a regular bool: the request handle is shared across middleware layers and we don't want to thread `&mut` through everything.
- JOLT-RS-021 (priority 21): two viable approaches for connecting RequestExt to a request lifecycle: (a) add `extensions: axum::http::Extensions` field to Request, store RequestExt there via Extensions::insert; (b) keep RequestExt as a separate parameter alongside Request in handlers. Approach (a) matches the PRD step's "axum request extension" language and the product_decision in prd.json (`req.markAsFinished → finished: AtomicBool`). The current `pub finished: bool` field on Request gets deleted at that point, and the JOLT-RS-014 `has_finished_reflects_finished_flag` test rewrites to use `RequestExt::mark_finished()` instead of `req.finished = true`.
- The Cargo.toml dependency surface is unchanged — `std::sync::atomic::AtomicBool` is in core, no new crate needed.
- `RequestExt` is currently `Send + Sync` automatically (AtomicBool is both). When 021 stores it in axum::http::Extensions, the `'static + Send + Sync` bound is satisfied. No PhantomData or unsafe needed.
- JsonBody openness lock from 018 is unaffected by this change. Phase04 doesn't touch the response surface.
- The `body_bytes` test helper is private to `tests::response` (same module). If `tests::request` or future test modules need similar bytes-extraction helpers, factor up to `mod tests` (sibling to `mod response`) — but only if a second consumer materializes; YAGNI applies.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-020: RequestExt mark_finished() + is_finished()

PRD item: JOLT-RS-020 (priority 20, phase04-requestext-flag) — Implement RequestExt::mark_finished() and RequestExt::is_finished().

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::request_ext` → 7/7 passed (2 prior + 5 new), 0 failed, 54 filtered out; finished in 0.00s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 61 passed total (up from 56); 0 failed.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.30s; no regressions.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..019 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Picked `Ordering::Relaxed` for both store and load per JOLT-RS-019 progress notes recommendation. `finished` is a one-way latch (false → true), no other state hangs off it, no acquire/release relationship to another datum. If a future requirement adds state that must be visible alongside the flip (e.g. a "finished_by" middleware-id), upgrade to Release/Acquire then — and update this comment so the next agent doesn't have to re-derive the choice.
- Both methods take `&self` (not `&mut self`). Locked in by `mark_finished_takes_shared_reference` test. The whole point of `AtomicBool` over `bool` is shared mutation across middleware layers without threading `&mut` through every call site; switching to `&mut self` would silently negate that.
- `mark_finished()` is `store(true, Relaxed)` not `compare_exchange(false, true, ..)`. Idempotent latch semantics are sufficient — there's no caller-visible difference between "first finisher" and "second finisher". A CAS would let middleware detect "I was the one who finished it," but no such caller exists yet and adding the API now would be premature. If JOLT-RS-021's middleware integration shows that detection matters, swap in `swap()` or a new `mark_finished_first() -> bool` then.
- Did NOT add `unmark_finished()` / reset semantics. The PRD treats this as a one-way latch (per JOLT-RS-019's notes: "false → true"). A reset method would invite middleware to un-finish a request, which contradicts the semantic. If a use case emerges (e.g. retry logic), a separate explicit `reset()` or a fresh `RequestExt::new()` is the right shape, not bidirectional toggling.
- Doc comment on `mark_finished()` explicitly states "Idempotent; subsequent calls are no-ops" — locked in by `mark_finished_is_idempotent` test. No doc on `is_finished()`: the name is self-explanatory and a docstring would just restate it.
- Did NOT introduce a `Finished` newtype or builder pattern. Bare AtomicBool with two methods is the minimal surface; adding wrappers would be premature abstraction the PRD doesn't request.
- Did NOT touch Request.finished (the deferred migration from JOLT-RS-014). That's JOLT-RS-021's scope when RequestExt gets wired through axum::http::Extensions.

Tests added (5 in `tests::request_ext`):
- `is_finished_is_false_after_construction` — `RequestExt::new().is_finished()` is false. Symmetric to the existing `new_constructs_with_finished_defaulting_to_false`, but exercises the new public method instead of the field.
- `mark_finished_flips_is_finished_to_true` — the PRD-mandated verification ("mark_finished() → is_finished() returns true").
- `mark_finished_is_idempotent` — calls mark_finished() twice; locks in latch semantics. Without this test, a future swap to `compare_exchange` that returns `Err` on already-set could pass silently if no one reasoned about the second-call path.
- `mark_finished_takes_shared_reference` — calls through `&ext` rather than `ext`; locks in the &self signature so a refactor to &mut self fails to compile.
- `is_finished_observes_direct_field_store` — stores via the public `finished` field with Ordering::Relaxed and reads via `is_finished()`. Proves the method reads the same atomic the field exposes; a refactor that introduces a shadow `cached_finished: bool` would fail this.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/request_ext.rs — added `mark_finished(&self)` and `is_finished(&self) -> bool`; imported `Ordering`.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added 5 unit tests in `mod request_ext`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-020 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-021 (priority 21, closes phase04): "Register RequestExt as an axum request extension type; test insertion + retrieval through Extensions." The deferred Request.finished migration from JOLT-RS-014 lands here. Two options for the integration shape:
  * (a) Add `extensions: axum::http::Extensions` field to Request, store `Arc<RequestExt>` (or `RequestExt` directly) via `Extensions::insert`. Aligns with PRD step's "axum request extension" language and the product_decision (`req.markAsFinished → finished: AtomicBool`). The `pub finished: bool` field on Request gets deleted at that point.
  * (b) Keep RequestExt as a separate parameter alongside Request in handlers. Simpler but less idiomatic — axum's typed Extensions are the canonical place.
  Recommend (a). When implementing, the JOLT-RS-014 `has_finished_reflects_finished_flag` test rewrites from `req.finished = true` to `req.extensions().get::<RequestExt>().unwrap().mark_finished()` (or whatever lookup shape lands).
- Storage shape inside Extensions: `axum::http::Extensions::insert<T: 'static + Send + Sync>(t: T)` requires `T: Clone` for `.get()` to return a reference (it doesn't actually need Clone for insert, but `Extensions` clones internally on some paths). RequestExt is `!Clone` (AtomicBool is !Clone by design — see JOLT-RS-019 notes). Two ways out: (i) wrap in `Arc<RequestExt>` so the Arc is what's stored; `.get::<Arc<RequestExt>>()` gives `&Arc<RequestExt>`, and `.mark_finished()` works through Deref. (ii) implement `Clone for RequestExt` via per-field `.load(Relaxed)` — but that loses the shared-state invariant the type exists for. Recommend (i): `Arc<RequestExt>` in Extensions.
- The Cargo.toml dependency surface for 021 needs `axum::http::Extensions` — already available transitively through axum (which is already a dep). No new crate needed.
- If JOLT-RS-022+ (server builder phase) ends up needing `Default for RequestExt`, derive it then; AtomicBool::default() is false, so it's safe — just hold off until a consumer actually asks per JOLT-RS-019's "overspecified" guidance.
- Latch ordering choice (Relaxed for both) is now a load-bearing decision. The progress entry above documents the reasoning so a future agent reviewing memory ordering doesn't re-derive from scratch.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-021: RequestExt registration through axum Extensions (closes phase04)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-021 (priority 21, phase04-requestext-flag) — Register RequestExt as an axum request extension type; test insertion + retrieval through Extensions.

Verification:
- `cargo test -p jolt-core -- tests::request_ext` → 11/11 passed (7 prior + 4 new in `tests::request_ext_extensions`); 0 failed; 54 filtered out.
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.18s; no regressions.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 65 passed total (up from 61); 0 failed.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..020 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Picked `Arc<RequestExt>` as the embedding shape in `axum::http::Extensions` per JOLT-RS-020 progress note recommendation. `axum::http::Extensions::insert<T>` requires `T: Clone + Send + Sync + 'static`; `RequestExt` is intentionally `!Clone` (AtomicBool's interior mutability would be silently duplicated by a per-field Clone), so wrapping in `Arc` is the path that preserves the shared-state invariant. Cloning the Arc still points at the same atomic — verified by `mark_through_one_handle_visible_through_another`.
- Did NOT add an `extensions` field to `Request` or migrate `Request.finished` (the deferred migration flagged in JOLT-RS-014 / JOLT-RS-020 notes). The PRD step is narrowly scoped to "register + test"; the broader Request surgery is integration work that belongs to a later task that actually wires RequestExt through the request lifecycle. Doing it speculatively now would touch the JOLT-RS-014 `has_finished_reflects_finished_flag` test for no PRD-step benefit and would risk diverging the Request shape from whatever the server-builder/router phase actually needs (JOLT-RS-022..034).
- Did NOT add helper methods on `RequestExt` for Extensions integration (e.g. `RequestExt::insert_into(&self, ext: &mut Extensions)`). The standard `Extensions::insert(Arc::new(RequestExt::new()))` / `Extensions::get::<Arc<RequestExt>>()` pattern is already minimal and idiomatic; a wrapper helper would just hide one line of code and add an indirection a future reader would have to chase. If a real call site materializes that uses this pattern in 3+ places, factor it then.
- Did NOT change `request_ext.rs` itself. The "registration" in the PRD step is the act of storing the type in Extensions, not a method on the type. Leaving `request_ext.rs` untouched keeps the production code surface invariant under this PRD step (only tests added) — easier to review and reason about.
- Tests live in a new `mod request_ext_extensions` sibling to `mod request_ext` (rather than extending `request_ext` itself). Rationale: `request_ext` is for unit tests of the type's intrinsic API; `request_ext_extensions` is integration with axum's Extensions container — semantically distinct, and the separate filter (`tests::request_ext_extensions`) is useful when iterating on either slice in isolation. The module-level docstring on the new module captures the Clone/!Clone reasoning so future agents don't have to re-derive.

Tests added (4 in `tests::request_ext_extensions`):
- `insert_then_get_returns_same_instance` — inserts an `Arc<RequestExt>`, retrieves via `Extensions::get::<Arc<RequestExt>>()`, asserts the retrieved Arc points at the same heap allocation (via `Arc::as_ptr` pointer-equality). Locks in that Extensions stores by-Arc and does not silently clone the inner RequestExt.
- `mark_finished_through_extensions_is_observable_on_retrieval` — the PRD-mandated verification ("insert RequestExt into Extensions, retrieve, mark finished, verify"). Inserts, retrieves, asserts `!is_finished()`, calls `mark_finished()` through the retrieved handle, retrieves a second time, asserts `is_finished()`. Proves the same atomic state survives across get() calls.
- `get_returns_none_when_not_inserted` — sanity check on the Option return; protects against a future accidental Default-injection that would silently produce a never-finished RequestExt for handlers that didn't go through middleware.
- `mark_through_one_handle_visible_through_another` — clone an outside `Arc<RequestExt>` handle, insert one clone into Extensions, mutate via the inside-Extensions handle, observe via the outside handle. Locks in the shared-state invariant that motivates the `Arc` choice. Without this test, a future refactor that switched to `RequestExt: Clone` (per-field load) would pass insert/retrieve tests silently while breaking the contract.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added `mod request_ext_extensions` with 4 unit tests.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-021 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- Phase04 is now closed. Phase05 (server-builder) starts at JOLT-RS-022. The deferred `Request.finished` migration is STILL deferred — it's not in any phase04 task and the next natural home is whichever phase05/phase06 task first needs handlers to read the finished flag through the request lifecycle (likely JOLT-RS-033/034 "Router Tower Service: implement tower::Service for Router; injects RequestExt into every incoming request before dispatch"). When that task lands, the rewrite is mechanical: delete `pub finished: bool` from Request, delete the `has_finished()` method, rewrite the JOLT-RS-014 `has_finished_reflects_finished_flag` test to insert `Arc<RequestExt>` into a request's Extensions and call `mark_finished()` through it, and switch any callers of `req.has_finished()` to `req.extensions.get::<Arc<RequestExt>>().map(|e| e.is_finished()).unwrap_or(false)` (or similar). Keep a single source of truth for the finished flag — don't keep both `Request.finished: bool` and `Arc<RequestExt>.finished: AtomicBool` in parallel.
- The Arc-wrapping choice is now a load-bearing public contract: middleware that wants to mark finished will look up `Arc<RequestExt>` (not bare `RequestExt`) from Extensions. The `request_ext_extensions` module-level docstring documents this so a future agent doesn't re-derive the Clone/!Clone reasoning.
- `Extensions::insert` returns `Option<T>` — the previous value if any was present. The current tests don't exercise that return value because phase04 has no concept of "replacing" a RequestExt (one-per-request lifecycle). If a future caller intentionally re-inserts (e.g. middleware that resets state for a sub-request), add a test then.
- `axum::http::Extensions` is re-exported from the `http` crate. The `use axum::http::Extensions;` import in tests works because axum already pulls in `http`. No Cargo.toml change needed.
- The 4 new tests are pure-sync (no `#[tokio::test]`); RequestExt mutation through Extensions is non-async by construction. If a future test needs an async context (e.g. exercising RequestExt across an `await` point in middleware), the Arc<RequestExt>: Send + Sync property already holds — no API change needed.
- Phase05 priority cluster (JOLT-RS-022..027) is server-builder scaffolding. JoltServer struct, builder methods, start(), endpoint registration. None of those touch RequestExt directly, so phase04 is fully self-contained as of this commit.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-022: JoltServer struct shape (opens phase05)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-022 (priority 22, phase05-server-builder) — Define JoltServer struct with fields: port (u16), threads (usize), cors_config (Option<CorsConfig>), tls_config (Option<TlsConfig>). Start with stub types.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-core` → clean in 0.60s; struct compiles (the PRD-mandated check).
- `cargo check --workspace` → all 5 crates check clean in 0.26s; no regressions.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 65 passed, 0 failed (unchanged from JOLT-RS-021 baseline; this step adds no tests).

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..021 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- Stubs are unit structs (`pub struct CorsConfig;` / `pub struct TlsConfig;`) rather than empty named-field structs (`struct X {}`) or zero-field tuple structs. Rationale: the PRD says "Start with stub types," meaning the goal is a nameable, constructible-as-a-marker shape that callers can put in `Option<_>`. Unit structs are the minimum surface — adding fields now would prejudge what CORS/TLS config carries (origins, headers, max-age vs. cert path, key path, SNI map, trust store), and Phase 2 (CORS) and Phase 6 (TLS) are the natural homes for that shape. A future fill-in is a non-breaking add of fields.
- Both stubs derive only `Debug`. No `Clone`, no `Default`. `Debug` is here because `JoltServer` derives it (Option<T: Debug> requires T: Debug). Skipped Clone because nothing in JOLT-RS-022..027 requires copying a config; if JOLT-RS-024's builder methods or JOLT-RS-027's tests need clone semantics, derive then. Skipped Default because JOLT-RS-023 explicitly defines `JoltServer::new()` with sensible defaults (port 8080, threads = num_cpus) — that's the construction story for this type, not `Default`.
- All four `JoltServer` fields are `pub`. Rationale: matches the existing crate convention (`Request`, `RequestExt`, `Response`, `Cookie` all expose `pub` fields), and JOLT-RS-023's verification ("JoltServer::new() has port=8080") implicitly requires field readability. If 024 chooses to wall this off behind builder methods, a future sweep can drop the visibility — easier to remove `pub` than to add it back.
- New file `jolt-core/src/server.rs` instead of inlining into `lib.rs` or extending an existing module. The lib.rs convention is one struct family per module file (cookie/method/request/request_ext/response/status). JoltServer + its config records are a coherent family that will grow (builder impl in 023/024, start in 025, endpoint registration in 026) — keeping it co-located in `server.rs` from the start avoids a later move-and-rename diff.
- Re-exported via `pub use server::{CorsConfig, JoltServer, TlsConfig};` in `lib.rs`, alphabetized with sibling re-exports. Three names instead of `pub use server::*` to match the existing per-symbol style — explicit re-exports document the public crate surface in one place.
- Did NOT add a `JoltServer::new()` or any impl block. That's JOLT-RS-023's scope. The PRD-step verification is "Struct compiles," and the priority-rule comment in prd.json (lower priority runs first) means each item is a discrete slice — bundling 023 here would conflate two reviewable units. If 023 turns out to need a different field shape (e.g., `tls_config` becomes `Arc<TlsConfig>` to share across spawned tasks), the diff scope stays small.
- Did NOT add tests. The PRD verification is "Struct compiles" (compile-check), not "tests pass." JOLT-RS-027 is the tests slice for phase05; adding tests here would steal scope from 027 and leave it under-defined. The downstream tests will exercise the public field surface naturally.
- Module-level docstring on `server.rs` notes that the stubs are placeholders to be filled in their respective phase tasks (CORS in phase 2, TLS in phase 6). This anchors the next agent so they don't try to flesh out CorsConfig/TlsConfig prematurely as part of phase05.
