The variant cost is negligible (one tag byte + the largest variant payload — `axum::Router` is already the size driver) and the `match &mut self.inner` in `call`/`poll_ready` adds one branch per request, which is well under the per-request boxed-future allocation already in the hot path. JOLT-RS-036 is the right time to collapse this back to a single variant if `from_axum` gets retired then.
- **`Router::from_registry(EndpointRegistry) -> Self` calls `registry.sort()` internally** before wrapping in `Arc`. PRD-034 says "match against sorted endpoint registry" — making `from_registry` responsible for the sort means callers can't accidentally bypass longest-path-first matching. The cost is one O(n log n) sort at construction (typically dozens of endpoints, not thousands); the benefit is the `Arc<EndpointRegistry>` is immutable from then on, which lines up with multi-task `Clone` distribution that JOLT-RS-035+ may use. Documented `longest_path_wins_when_multiple_registered` test pins the contract.
- **Constructor name: `from_registry` (not `new`).** PRD-036 reserves `Router::new(registry: EndpointRegistry)` as the primary public constructor. Naming this constructor `new` now would force a rename in 036 and break callers; `from_registry` mirrors the existing `from_axum` shape and is a natural lower-level entry that can stay alongside `new` once 036 lands (or get retired if 036 is the only blessed entry).
- **`call` flow: inject `Arc<RequestExt>` first, then dispatch.** RequestExt insertion is unconditional across both Inner variants — same contract as JOLT-RS-033, and the 3 existing 033 tests still cover the injection invariant via the `Inner::Axum` path. The injection happens BEFORE the inner match so a future `Inner` variant doesn't have to remember to do it.
- **Method parsing failure → 404.** `req.method().as_str().parse::<Method>()` returns `Err` for unsupported verbs (CONNECT, TRACE, custom methods). Per PRD step text "On no match, return 404", an unparseable method cannot match any `Method`-keyed registry entry, so the structural answer is 404. Used `let-else` to short-circuit before the per-iteration loop allocation.
- **Method-mismatch on a registered path also returns 404 (not 405) at the 034 layer.** PRD-034 step text says "On no match, return 404." — both unknown paths and method mismatches are "no match" by that rule. JOLT-RS-037's verification explicitly calls for 405 on method mismatch, which means 037 will refine this behavior (likely by tracking "path matched, method didn't" during the walk and choosing the response based on which mismatch came up). The `method_mismatch_on_registered_path_returns_404` test pins the current contract so 037 sees a focused break point rather than a confusing test-set rewrite.
- **Walk shape: `for endpoint in registry.iter() { if path && method match → dispatch }`.** O(n) per request, O(1) early exit on match. Could be optimized later (HashMap keyed on (path, method), trie, etc.) — measure first. The walk is intentionally simple to make JOLT-RS-035's finished-flag short-circuit easy to slot in (one extension-read between match and dispatch) and JOLT-RS-037's 405 differentiation a small refactor (track path-only-match flag during the loop).
- **`build_jolt_request` visibility: changed from `pub(crate)`-by-default-of-being-in-the-same-module to explicit `pub(crate)`.** The function lives in `endpoint_registry.rs` because that's where `build_router`'s closures need it; router.rs now also needs it for the dispatch path. Two options: (a) make it `pub(crate)`, (b) move to a shared adapter module. Picked (a) because it's the minimum-churn move and the function's contract ("axum→jolt request snapshot at dispatch time") is identical for both call sites. If a third caller appears, that's the trigger for option (b) — likely the new module would be `request.rs::Request::from_axum`, which generalizes naturally to a method.
- **`not_found()` helper builds a fresh empty-body 404 every call** rather than caching a static one. The `axum::response::Response` type wraps `Body`, which contains an internal `Bytes` that's not `'static`-clonable across the type's API. Building per-call is cheap (one `Bytes::new()` + one header insertion) and avoids any unsafe cell/`OnceCell<Body>` plumbing. If profiling shows this is hot, the right move is a `Bytes::new()`-backed const, not an LRU.
- **Did NOT add `Default for Router`.** Same rationale as JOLT-RS-033: no clippy gate yet, and the constructor surface is still moving (036 will land `new(registry)`). Default could derive cleanly post-036 via `Router::new(EndpointRegistry::default())`.
- **Five tests under nested `mod registry_dispatch` inside `mod router`.** Submodule keeps the 034 tests groupable as `cargo test -- tests::router::registry_dispatch` and avoids polluting the parent module's namespace. Tests cover: (1) `registered_get_hello_returns_200` — verbatim PRD verification half 1, with body assertion to prove dispatch reached the actual handler not just a generic 200; (2) `unknown_path_returns_404` — verbatim PRD verification half 2; (3) `empty_registry_returns_404_for_any_request` — proves the zero-entries walk path is structurally correct (separate from "walked all entries, none matched"); (4) `method_mismatch_on_registered_path_returns_404` — pins the 034 contract that method mismatch is a 404 not a 405 (will flip with 037); (5) `longest_path_wins_when_multiple_registered` — pins that `from_registry` calls sort() so `/api/hello` beats `/api`, locking in the longest-path-first invariant the PRD step requires.
- Test fixture: reused the `EchoEndpoint { path, method, body }` shape from `mod endpoint_registry::build_router`. Same rationale as that submodule — single parameterized struct yields N distinct routes for N tests. Did NOT factor it out to a shared parent fixture because the two submodules' assertions diverge (build_router tests assert on the `axum::Router` directly; registry_dispatch tests assert on the `Router` wrapper), and the duplication is small enough to keep colocated with each test set.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/router.rs — `Router` storage now an `Inner` enum (`Axum(axum::Router) | Registry(Arc<EndpointRegistry>)`); kept `from_axum` for 033 + introduced `from_registry` (calls `sort()` then `Arc::new`); reworked `Service::call` to inject `Arc<RequestExt>` then dispatch via the matched variant; added `not_found()` helper; updated module docstring with the phase07 ladder. New imports: `axum::body::Body`, `axum::http::StatusCode`, `crate::endpoint_registry::{build_jolt_request, EndpointRegistry}`, `crate::method::Method`.
- jolt-core/src/endpoint_registry.rs — `build_jolt_request` is now `pub(crate)` (was implicit-private); added doc-comment naming both call sites (`build_router` closures + `Router::call`).
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — new `mod registry_dispatch` inside `mod router` with 5 tests covering the PRD-mandated verification + walk-shape invariants.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-034 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-035 (priority 35, finished-flag short-circuit): plugs into Router::call's dispatch loop. The natural insertion point is between the (path, method) match and `endpoint.handler(jolt_req).await`: `if req.extensions().get::<Arc<RequestExt>>().is_some_and(|e| e.is_finished()) { return Ok(...skip-handler response...); }`. The "skip-handler response" is the open question — does the short-circuit return 200 with empty body, or does it propagate whatever response the finishing middleware produced? PRD-035's step text ("if RequestExt is finished, return response immediately without calling handler") suggests there's a response captured somewhere; likely RequestExt grows a `response: Mutex<Option<Response>>` field, and 035 also adds the read path. Recommend deciding when 035 starts — the answer affects whether RequestExt stays bool-only or grows.
- JOLT-RS-036 (`Router::new(registry: EndpointRegistry) -> Self`): straightforward alias for `from_registry`. Open question: collapse `Inner` to a single variant by retiring `from_axum`? If 035/036 don't end up using the `Inner::Axum` path, retiring it shrinks the type and removes a per-request branch in `call`. Reckon: retire it. The 033 tests can be rewritten to use registry-based fixtures; the injection contract they verify is preserved by Router::call's unconditional `extensions_mut().insert(...)` regardless of which dispatch backend runs.
- JOLT-RS-037 (test sweep): path matching (covered), 404 unknown (covered), 405 method-mismatch (NOT covered — currently 404; needs a small refactor in `call` to track "saw a path-match-but-method-miss during the walk" and return 405 if all path-mismatches were misses), finished-flag short-circuit (covered by 035). The `EchoEndpoint` fixture in `mod registry_dispatch` is the natural reuse target; `mod registry_dispatch` will likely get renamed or split.
- The `Inner` enum's `Inner::Axum` variant is currently only used by JOLT-RS-033's tests. If 035/036/037 don't grow new use cases for it, it's the right call to retire it during 036 (see above). If a use case does emerge (e.g. mounting a third-party axum::Router for static-asset serving), the variant pays for itself.
- The `not_found()` helper builds the 404 body per-call. Two callers today (the unparseable-method short-circuit + the no-match end-of-loop branch). If a third site appears (e.g. JOLT-RS-035's short-circuit response shape), centralize on a `crate::response::not_found()` instead of a router-local helper.
- `build_jolt_request`'s home in `endpoint_registry.rs` is starting to look wrong now that `router.rs` also calls it. If a third call site appears, move it to `request.rs` as `Request::from_axum(axum_req).await -> Self`. Don't move yet — premature.
- Method parsing for `req.method()` swallows unknown verbs into 404. If a future PRD wants to surface 501 Not Implemented for unknown verbs (RFC 9110 §15.6.2 says 501 is the canonical response for an unrecognized method), the change is one-line: replace the `Ok(not_found())` with a 501-builder. Not a JOLT-RS-034 concern.
- Sort responsibility: `from_registry` calls sort. If a future caller wants un-sorted iteration order (e.g. for deterministic test reproduction of registration order), expose a `from_unsorted_registry` escape hatch — but only if a real use case shows up.
- JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict test) is still the only phase05 holdout. Same ~10-line shape from prior progress notes.
- JOLT-RS-032 (endpoint-registry test bundle) is still on the same wait — duplicate-path detection design choice + path-param extraction Request-field decision both still open. Recommend tackling alongside JOLT-RS-037 once method-mismatch 405 is wired (the test bundles overlap heavily).

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-035: finished-flag short-circuit + preserve-existing RequestExt contract

PRD item: JOLT-RS-035 (priority 35, phase07-router-tower-service) — Integrate finished-flag check: after each response, if RequestExt is finished, return response immediately without calling handler.

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 035 is the next architectural item in the phase07 ladder. JOLT-RS-036 ("Router::new(registry)") and JOLT-RS-037 (test sweep) both inherit from this contract; landing 035 first fixes the shape of `Arc<RequestExt>` flow through the dispatch loop so 036 is just a constructor rename and 037 is a test refinement. JOLT-RS-027/032 are polish/test bundles with no upstream dependencies.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-core` → clean in 0.64s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib -- tests::router` → 13/13 passed (3 prior 033 tests still passing under their renamed counterparts + 5 prior 034 dispatch tests + 5 new 035 tests covering stashed-response short-circuit, fallback-to-500, preserve-existing-not-finished, finished-without-route-match, and the renamed preserve-existing test), 91 filtered out, 0.00s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib -- tests::request_ext` → 17/17 passed (11 prior latch tests + 6 new stash tests covering set/take/drain/replace/independence-from-mark_finished), 87 filtered out, 0.00s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 104 passed total (up from 93); 0 failed; 0 ignored.
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.35s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..034 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **Inverted JOLT-RS-033's overwrite-on-call contract.** The 033 progress notes explicitly named this as the "non-obvious correctness invariant" and pinned it with `service_call_overwrites_caller_supplied_request_ext`; that test was provisional, locking in the temporary state until 035 landed the actual short-circuit. With this PRD item, Router::call now PRESERVES a caller-supplied `Arc<RequestExt>` if one is already in extensions and only inserts a fresh one when no upstream layer has done so. The "abuse prevention" rationale the 033 note cited was always weak — Router::call is an internal API; only middleware reaches it, and the whole point of `AtomicBool` for the latch is shared mutation across the chain. Overwriting would strand any upstream `mark_finished()` and force every middleware to re-derive its own state. The renamed test (`service_call_preserves_caller_supplied_request_ext`) uses `Arc::ptr_eq` against the original handle — a value-only assertion ("the latch is/isn't set") would pass coincidentally even if a regression re-introduced the overwrite, so the identity check is the load-bearing assertion. Added a sibling test (`service_call_inserts_fresh_request_ext_when_none_supplied`) to pin the other half of the contract.
- **`RequestExt` grew a `response: Mutex<Option<Response>>` field with `set_response`/`take_response` accessors.** This is the stash that the Router-level short-circuit takes when a finishing middleware wants to dictate the actual response body+status. Open question from the 034 progress notes: "does RequestExt grow a response: Mutex<Option<Response>> field, and does 035 also add the read path?" — answered yes to both. `axum::response::Response` is not `Clone` (the inner `Body` carries a stream), so the stash is a single-shot move; `take()` semantics are pinned by `take_response_drains_the_stash`. The Mutex is `std::sync::Mutex` (not `parking_lot`) — no other workspace crate depends on parking_lot today, and stdlib is the simplest default; if profiling shows Mutex contention is a real cost, the swap is one line.
- **`set_response` and `mark_finished` are deliberately independent.** A middleware that wants to stash a response without committing to short-circuit (e.g. a default body that downstream layers can override before any layer marks finished) shouldn't be forced into a finished latch. Symmetrically, `mark_finished()` doesn't clear the stash — the canonical pattern is `ext.set_response(...); ext.mark_finished();`, and reordering or split-call layering must not race the latch against the stash. Two tests pin both directions (`set_response_does_not_implicitly_mark_finished`, `mark_finished_does_not_clear_a_previously_stashed_response`).
- **Last-writer-wins on `set_response`.** A later layer (e.g. an error mapper running after auth) that wants to override an earlier stash shouldn't have to reach into the option directly. `set_response_replaces_a_previously_stashed_response` pins it.
- **`response: Mutex<Option<Response>>` field is private; access is via methods.** The existing `pub finished: AtomicBool` field stays public for compat with the 11 prior tests that read it directly via `ext.finished.load(...)` / `ext.finished.into_inner()`; converting those to method calls is a separate cleanup, not in scope for 035. New field was made private from the start because there are no existing direct-field call sites and methods give us the freedom to swap the storage shape later (e.g. swap Mutex for an unsync RefCell behind a Send shim) without breaking callers.
- **`RequestExt: Send + Sync` preserved.** `AtomicBool: Send + Sync`; `Mutex<T>: Send + Sync` when `T: Send` (not `T: Sync`); `axum::response::Response: Send`. So `Mutex<Option<Response>>: Send + Sync` and the wrapping `Arc<RequestExt>` is still `Send` (which the boxed-future-with-+Send bound on Service::Future requires).
- **`#[derive(Debug)]` retained.** `Mutex<Option<Response>>: Debug` because `axum::response::Response = http::Response<axum::body::Body>` and both `http::Response: Debug` (when body is Debug) and `axum::body::Body: Debug` are satisfied. No manual impl needed.
- **Two short-circuit checks in Router::call (early + pre-handler).** The early check (right after RequestExt resolution, before the registry walk) is the optimization: it avoids `build_jolt_request`'s body-buffering work for a request whose outcome is already decided, and it ensures a finishing-middleware-without-route-match scenario surfaces the stashed response (e.g. 403) instead of a 404 (`finished_flag_short_circuits_even_when_path_does_not_match` pins this). The pre-handler re-check is a future-proofing checkpoint: a later inner-middleware tier (post-035, pre-046) may finish the request between the route walk and the handler invocation, and the second check ensures Router still honors that. Cost is one atomic load — zero on the hot path.
- **`short_circuit_response` helper falls back to 500 when the stash is empty.** A middleware that calls `mark_finished()` without `set_response()` is a bug — surfacing 500 (rather than 200 or whatever the matched handler would have returned) makes the bug visible at the boundary instead of letting it propagate as a misleading success. `finished_flag_without_stashed_response_falls_back_to_500` pins it. The 500 body is empty, matching `not_found()`'s body shape; if a future PRD wants to surface a JSON error body here, that's a `crate::response` concern, not a Router-local one.
- **PRD-mandated verification (`finished_flag_with_stashed_response_short_circuits_handler`)** uses an `AtomicBool` invocation tracker instead of a panicking handler. tokio's runtime can sometimes catch panics in async tasks and turn them into runtime errors that surface as test failures with confusing diagnostics; the AtomicBool flag gives a direct, panic-free assertion that `handler must not be invoked when RequestExt is finished`. Asserts response status (401), response body (the stashed "auth required" string — which proves the body actually reached the wire, not just the status), and `!invoked` together so any one regression makes the failure obvious.
- **`caller_supplied_not_finished_request_ext_dispatches_normally` test.** The third leaf of the JOLT-RS-035 contract: a caller-supplied not-finished RequestExt must NOT short-circuit. Without this test, a regression that toggled the finished check sense ("if !is_finished") would still pass the two finishing tests above (they happen to use `is_finished()=true`) and the `service_call_preserves_caller_supplied_request_ext` test (which doesn't go through the registry path).
- **Did NOT add an inner-middleware system or extend the Endpoint trait.** Both were tempting paths for the test design but explicitly out of scope: phase11 (`AutoMiddleware` derive macro) is the right place for inner-middleware composition, and Endpoint-trait extensions would touch every other crate. The current shape — Router preserves Arc<RequestExt>, outer tower::Layer middleware mutates the shared latch — is the canonical tower pattern and matches what spec_rust.md §"Key Design Decisions" #1 calls out: "Tower middleware layers with a `RequestExt` extension that carries a `finished: bool` flag. Each layer checks this before proceeding."
- **Did NOT update `Request::has_finished` / `Request::finished` field.** The `Request` struct still carries its own `pub finished: bool` field (legacy from JOLT-RS-014). That field is independent of `Arc<RequestExt>` and is read by `Request::has_finished()`. Migration to a unified flag (drop `Request::finished`, point `has_finished` at the `RequestExt` lookup) is a separate refactor — likely alongside the `build_jolt_request` move flagged in JOLT-RS-034's progress notes. Out of scope for 035.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/request_ext.rs — added private `response: Mutex<Option<Response>>` field; added `set_response(&self, Response)` and `take_response(&self) -> Option<Response>` methods; updated `RequestExt::new()` to default the stash to `None`; updated module docstring to name the stash. New imports: `std::sync::Mutex`, `axum::response::Response`.
- jolt-core/src/router.rs — Router::call now preserves a caller-supplied `Arc<RequestExt>` (replaces unconditional overwrite); added early finished-flag check before registry walk and pre-handler re-check inside the loop; added `short_circuit_response` helper that takes the stash or falls back to 500. Updated module docstring to name the new contract.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added 6 new tests under `mod request_ext` (set/take/drain/replace/mark_finished-independence/take-on-empty); replaced `service_call_overwrites_caller_supplied_request_ext` with `service_call_preserves_caller_supplied_request_ext` (Arc::ptr_eq identity check) and added sibling `service_call_inserts_fresh_request_ext_when_none_supplied`; added 4 new tests under `mod registry_dispatch` (stashed-401, fallback-500, not-finished dispatches normally, finished-without-route-match returns stash). Imported `std::sync::Arc` into `mod registry_dispatch` for the new tests.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-035 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-036 (priority 36, `Router::new(registry: EndpointRegistry) -> Self` constructor): now a straightforward alias for `from_registry`. Open question from 034's notes is still open: collapse `Inner` to a single variant by retiring `from_axum`? The 033 tests (all 3 of them) still ride on `Inner::Axum`, so retiring it means rewriting them to use registry-based fixtures. Recommend retiring during 036 — the injection contract those tests verify (preserve-or-insert) is now uniformly enforced before the variant match in `call`, so registry-based fixtures cover the same surface. If retiring, also retire the `Inner` enum entirely (single-variant enum is dead code).
- JOLT-RS-037 (test sweep): path matching (covered), 404 unknown (covered), 405 method-mismatch (NOT covered — currently 404; needs `call` to track "saw a path-match-but-method-miss during the walk" and return 405 if all matches were method-misses), finished-flag short-circuit (covered by 035 — likely a no-op for 037). The `EchoEndpoint` fixture in `mod registry_dispatch` is the natural reuse target.
- The `pub finished: AtomicBool` field on RequestExt is still publicly accessible. The 11 prior tests that read it directly via `ext.finished.load(...)` / `ext.finished.into_inner()` haven't been migrated to method-call form; that's a separate cleanup. If a future PRD wants to make the field private, the migration is a `replace_all` on the read sites + some test rewrites. Not urgent.
- The pre-handler re-check inside the registry loop (`if request_ext.is_finished()` between match and dispatch) is currently dead code in production: nothing inside Router::call between the early check and the dispatch can finish the request. It's load-bearing for future inner-middleware that runs between match and dispatch (post-035, pre-046). If JOLT-RS-046+ ends up putting all middleware OUTSIDE Router::call (as outer tower::Layer wrappers around the whole Router), the pre-handler re-check can be removed. Don't remove until that decision lands.
- The `short_circuit_response` 500 fallback uses an empty body. If/when a JSON error response convention lands (likely as part of `crate::response::Response<E>` where `E: JsonBody`), centralize on a `crate::response::internal_server_error()` helper. Two callers today (the registry-loop check and the early check) both go through this one helper, so the migration is one site.
- `set_response` / `take_response` use `std::sync::Mutex`. If profiling later shows lock contention is a real cost (unlikely — there's at most one writer per request), swap to `parking_lot::Mutex` (no poison handling, ~3x faster on Linux). Not yet justified; stdlib is the simplest default.
- `RequestExt::Default` is still not derived. With the new field, `Mutex<Option<Response>>: Default` (None default), so a derived `Default` would work. No call site asks for it; defer until one does.
- JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict test) is still the only phase05 holdout. Same ~10-line shape from prior progress notes.
- JOLT-RS-032 (endpoint-registry test bundle): same wait — duplicate-path detection design choice + path-param extraction Request-field decision both still open. Worth tackling alongside 037.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-036: Router::new(registry) canonical constructor

PRD item: JOLT-RS-036 (priority 36, phase07-router-tower-service) — `Router::new(registry: EndpointRegistry) -> Self` constructor with optional tower Layer stack.

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 036 is the next phase07 architectural item. It locks in the canonical constructor name (`Router::new`) that JOLT-RS-037's test sweep + every downstream phase that constructs a Router (server wiring, auto-middleware codegen, integration tests) will write against. Landing it now means downstream callers don't accumulate `from_registry` references that need a rename later. JOLT-RS-027/032 remain polish/test bundles with no upstream dependencies.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-core` → clean in 0.66s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib -- tests::router` → 16/16 passed (3 prior 033 tests + 9 prior 034/035 dispatch tests + 3 new 036 tests covering the canonical constructor end-to-end + the inherited longest-path-first sort + tower::ServiceBuilder composability), 91 filtered out, 0.00s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 107 passed total (up from 104); 0 failed; 0 ignored.
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.28s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..035 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **`Router::new` is a thin delegate to `Router::from_registry` (one line).** The PRD step asks for `Router::new(registry: EndpointRegistry) -> Self`; `from_registry` already does exactly the right work (sort + Arc-wrap + variant select). Re-implementing the body inline in `new` would duplicate the sort-then-Arc construction and create a second site that future changes to construction (e.g. accepting a pre-sorted registry, switching `Inner` storage) would have to keep in lockstep. The delegate keeps the single source of truth in `from_registry` and lets `new` stand purely for the naming/discovery surface.
- **Did NOT retire `from_registry` or `from_axum`.** JOLT-RS-035's progress notes recommended retiring `from_axum` during 036 (so `Inner` collapses to a single variant). Did not do this because (a) it's strictly out of scope for the PRD step text, which only asks to add `new`, and the auto-prompt's "Keep the change small and focused" rule overrides the deferred recommendation; (b) the 3 existing 033 tests that ride on `Inner::Axum` would need rewriting and that's a separate, larger change with its own decisions (which fixture do the rewritten 033 tests use? do they merge with the registry_dispatch fixtures?); (c) `from_registry` may stay useful as a more explicit name for callers that want to disambiguate from `axum::Router::new` in scopes where both types are imported. If a future PRD wants to retire `from_axum` (and possibly `from_registry`), it gets its own progress entry. Documented this explicitly in `from_registry`'s rustdoc so the next reader sees the relationship.
- **Did NOT add a Router-side `.layer()` method.** The PRD step text says "with optional tower Layer stack." Two readings: (a) Router's API exposes `.layer()` for chained tower composition, à la axum::Router; (b) Router IS a tower::Service so callers stack layers around it externally via `tower::ServiceBuilder`. Picked (b) because (a) requires non-trivial type-erasure plumbing — a stored `BoxCloneSyncService` would force every `call` to dispatch through a vtable instead of the existing direct match-on-`Inner`, doubling the per-request indirection cost for a feature no current caller uses. Reading (b) is also more idiomatic tower (every tower::Service can be layered externally; only frameworks that want to centralize layer ergonomics for users add type-erased `.layer()` methods). The `new_constructor_composes_with_tower_service_builder` test pins this contract by routing through `ServiceBuilder::new().service(router)`. If a future PRD wants Router-side `.layer()`, it'll be its own redesign — likely landing alongside or after JOLT-RS-046 when middleware composition has a richer API to fit into.
- **Module docstring "ladder for phase07" updated to mark 035 as landed and 036 as the current entry.** Keeps the in-file phase tracker synchronized with prd.json so a reader landing in `router.rs` cold sees the current state without having to cross-reference. Same convention as 034/035's docstring updates.
- **Three new tests, all under `mod registry_dispatch`** (not a sibling submodule):
  1. `new_constructor_yields_ready_to_serve_router` — verbatim PRD verification ("Router::new() yields ready-to-serve axum Router") translated to "Router::new(registry) drives a registered route end-to-end with 200 + body match." The body assertion is load-bearing: a regression that returned 200 with an empty body (e.g. dispatched to a no-op handler instead of the registered one) would still pass status-only assertions.
  2. `new_constructor_sorts_registry_for_longest_path_match` — pins that `new` delegates to `from_registry` and inherits the longest-path-first sort. Without this test, a regression that had `new` skip the sort (e.g. wrapping the registry in `Arc` directly without calling `sort()` first) would compile and pass the basic test, then silently route to the shorter handler. Mirrors `longest_path_wins_when_multiple_registered` but on the `new` constructor surface so the contract is independently observable for both entry points.
  3. `new_constructor_composes_with_tower_service_builder` — pins the "optional tower Layer stack" interpretation: Router is a tower::Service, so `ServiceBuilder::new().service(router)` works with no `.layer(...)` calls (identity ServiceBuilder is the ground case for arbitrary `.layer(...)` chains). The test would fail to compile if Router stopped implementing `Service<AxumRequest, Response = Response, Error = Infallible>` (e.g. if a future change introduced a fallible Service::Error or changed the Response type), surfacing the regression at type-check time rather than runtime.
- **Did NOT add a Router-side `.layer()` test, since there's no `.layer()` method to test.** A test that wraps Router in a non-trivial layer (e.g. `tower::ServiceBuilder::new().layer(SomeLayer).service(router)`) would prove the same composability fact as the identity test but require either a custom Layer impl in the test or pulling in a tower feature crate (e.g. `tower::limit::ConcurrencyLimitLayer` requires the `limit` feature, which jolt-core's Cargo.toml doesn't enable). The identity-ServiceBuilder test is the smallest sufficient artifact; if a future test needs to demonstrate non-identity composition, a custom Layer fixture is one struct + one impl.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/router.rs — added `Router::new(registry: EndpointRegistry) -> Self` as a thin delegate to `from_registry`; updated module docstring to mark 035 landed and 036 current; added rustdoc on the `new` constructor explaining the "optional tower Layer stack" semantics + showing the `ServiceBuilder::new().layer(...).service(router)` composition pattern; tightened `from_registry` rustdoc to point callers at `new`.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — added 3 new tests under `mod registry_dispatch` covering the canonical constructor end-to-end (`new_constructor_yields_ready_to_serve_router`), inherited longest-path-first sort (`new_constructor_sorts_registry_for_longest_path_match`), and tower::ServiceBuilder composability (`new_constructor_composes_with_tower_service_builder` — uses `tower::ServiceBuilder` directly).
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-036 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-037 (priority 37, test sweep): path matching (covered), 404 unknown (covered), 405 method-mismatch (NOT covered — currently 404; needs `call` to track "saw a path-match-but-method-miss during the walk" and return 405 if all matches were method-misses), finished-flag short-circuit (covered by 035 — likely a no-op for 037). The `EchoEndpoint` fixture in `mod registry_dispatch` is the natural reuse target. Recommend doing the 405 refinement in `Router::call`'s registry loop: replace the early-return on a (path, method) match with a flag "saw_path_match" that defaults false and flips when path matches but method doesn't; after the walk, if no match was dispatched but `saw_path_match`, return 405 instead of 404. Two-line change; one new test.
- The `from_axum` retirement question (deferred from 035 + this iteration): still open. Recommend creating its own PRD item or absorbing it into 037 as a "tests sweep + cleanup" — the test rewrites are the bulk of the work, and they overlap with 037's test surface. If absorbed, also retire the `Inner` enum and replace it with a bare `Arc<EndpointRegistry>` field; this drops one branch from `call`'s hot path and shrinks the type by a tag byte.
- `Router::new` and `Router::from_registry` are now siblings with identical behavior. If both stick around long-term, consider re-examining whether `from_registry` adds value vs just `new`. For now, the doc cross-reference makes the relationship explicit. If a future signature divergence appears (e.g. `from_registry` accepts a pre-sorted registry while `new` always sorts), that's the trigger to keep both; otherwise drop `from_registry` when convenient.
- Tower Layer stacking is currently an EXTERNAL composition pattern (`ServiceBuilder::new().layer(L).service(router)`). If a future PRD wants Router-side `.layer()` for ergonomics, the design has two paths: (a) type-erased storage via `BoxCloneSyncService` (one vtable hop per request, idiomatic for runtime-composed stacks), or (b) a generic `Router<S>` parameter that tracks the layered service type at the type level (zero-cost but requires every Router consumer to be generic over S, including JoltServer). Worth deciding before the auto-middleware phase (10/11) lands, since middleware codegen will likely prefer one path or the other.
- The 3 new 036 tests live under `mod registry_dispatch` rather than getting their own `mod constructor` submodule, because they share the same `EchoEndpoint` fixture and assertions as the rest of the registry_dispatch tests. If `mod registry_dispatch` grows past ~15 tests, splitting by concern (constructor / dispatch / short-circuit) becomes worthwhile; not yet.
- JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict test) is still the only phase05 holdout. Same ~10-line shape from prior progress notes.
- JOLT-RS-032 (endpoint-registry test bundle): same wait — duplicate-path detection design choice + path-param extraction Request-field decision both still open. Worth tackling alongside 037.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-037: 405 method-mismatch refinement + Router test sweep

PRD item: JOLT-RS-037 (priority 37, phase07-router-tower-service) — Router unit test sweep covering path matching, 404 for unknown paths, 405 for method mismatch, and finished-flag short-circuit. Closes phase07.

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 037 is not pure polish — the step text mandates 405 for method mismatches, which is a real behavior change in `Router::call` (the registry walk now distinguishes path-hit-from-verb-miss). Landing it now also closes phase07 cleanly so phase08 (endpoint macro parsing, JOLT-RS-038+) can start against a stable router contract. JOLT-RS-027/032 remain polish/test bundles with no upstream dependencies.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-core` → clean in 0.71s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib -- tests::router` → 20/20 passed (the 16 prior 033..036 tests + 4 new 037 tests covering 405-on-mismatch, Allow-header-single-method, Allow-header-multi-method, unknown-path-still-404-not-405, and unparseable-verb-still-404), 91 filtered out, 0.00s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-core --lib` → 111 passed total (up from 107); 0 failed; 0 ignored.
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.43s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..036 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **Two-pass collapse, single-walk implementation.** The registry walk now collects path-match-method-miss entries into a `Vec<Method>` (allocated lazily — `Vec::new()` doesn't allocate until the first push, so the happy path stays allocation-free) while looking for the dispatch target in the same loop. Considered a true two-pass approach (first pass: dispatch-or-collect; second pass: emit Allow header from the collected methods), but it doubled the iteration cost on the hot path and offered no clarity benefit — the single loop with `if endpoint.path() == path { if endpoint.method() == method { dispatch } else { collect } }` reads cleanly and walks the registry exactly once. The PRD-036 progress notes recommended "two-line change; one new test"; the actual landed shape is closer to ten lines (including the 405 helper + the conservative-404 retention for unparseable verbs) but the two-line version would have skipped the Allow header which RFC 9110 §15.5.6 mandates with MUST-strength.
- **`Allow` header is comma-separated, registry-insertion-ordered.** RFC 9110 §10.2.1 specifies comma-separated; order isn't normative. Picked stable insertion order because (a) it's what `EndpointRegistry::sort` (which uses `sort_by_key` under the hood — stable per the standard library guarantee) gives us for free, and (b) test assertions need a deterministic listing or they'd be flake-prone. The deterministic-order test (`method_mismatch_returns_405_with_allow_listing_all_registered_methods`) pins this contract — a regression that switched to an unstable sort or HashMap-based collection would surface as `assert_eq!(allow, "GET, POST")` failing with a flipped order.
- **Unparseable HTTP verbs (CONNECT/TRACE/etc) still surface 404, NOT 405.** Two readings of "method not allowed" were on the table: (a) "no registered endpoint accepts this verb on this path" (which would surface 405 with the path's allowed methods listed in the Allow header), or (b) "this verb is something Jolt doesn't understand at all" (which would surface 501 Not Implemented per RFC 9110 §15.6.2, OR 404 to keep the framework's verb vocabulary opaque). Picked (b)+404 because (a) leaks Jolt's vocabulary to a caller that already sent something Jolt doesn't speak (e.g. CONNECT for an HTTP tunnel — surfacing "GET is allowed here" in response to a CONNECT is misleading) and the conservative answer is to treat the request as unhandled. Pinned by `unparseable_http_verb_returns_404_even_for_registered_path`. If a future PRD wants 501 for unparseable verbs, the change is one line — replace `Ok(not_found())` in the early `Method::from_str` branch with a 501-builder.
- **404 must NOT carry an `Allow` header.** Pinned by `unknown_path_returns_404_not_405_even_when_registry_is_populated`. Without this assertion, a regression that flipped the inner conditional (`if endpoint.method() == method` → `if endpoint.method() != method`) would still pass the unknown-path test (since `path != "/missing"` short-circuits the outer `if`), but break the "no path match" leaf of the contract. The Allow-header-absence assertion catches a different regression class than the 404-status assertion alone.
- **`pre-handler is_finished()` re-check stays in scope.** The check between the route walk and `endpoint.handler(jolt_req).await` is dead code today (nothing inside `Router::call` between the early check and the dispatch can finish the request), and one might argue it should be removed once 037 lands. Kept it because (a) phase11's `AutoMiddleware` will likely run user-defined inner middleware between match and dispatch, at which point this check goes from dead-code to load-bearing, and (b) the cost is one atomic load per dispatch — zero on the 405/404 paths that bypass it. Adding it back later would be easy; leaving it now is one fewer thing to remember.
- **Replaced the provisional `method_mismatch_on_registered_path_returns_404` test, didn't keep both.** The 034-era test was explicitly provisional — its docstring named JOLT-RS-037 as the inflection point. Keeping it alongside the new `_returns_405` test would create a flat-out contradiction (same fixture, opposite expectations) and force one of them to live behind `#[ignore]` or `#[cfg]`. Replacement is the right move — the historical fact that the contract was once 404 lives in git history + this progress.txt entry.
- **Did NOT centralize `not_found()` / `method_not_allowed()` in a `crate::response` module.** Two helpers in router.rs is fine. The progress note in 034 flagged centralization "if a third site appears" — the third site is `short_circuit_response`'s 500 fallback (already inline in router.rs). All three are router-local. If/when phase13 (body-parsing) adds a 400 for malformed JSON, that's the natural trigger to extract `crate::response::{not_found, method_not_allowed, internal_server_error, bad_request}`; not yet.
- **`Allow` header value is built via `String::join`, not `HeaderValue::from_str` + iterative concat.** A naive `methods.iter().fold(String::new(), |acc, m| acc + ...)` would work but be quadratic in the number of methods (each fold step reallocates). `Vec<&str>::join` is linear — even if no path is ever expected to register more than ~7 methods, the linear shape is the right default. The performance difference is microscopic in absolute terms; the choice is about not writing surprising-shape code.
- **`method_not_allowed` builds a 405 with empty body.** Matches the shape of `not_found()` and `short_circuit_response`'s 500 fallback. Considered surfacing a JSON error body (`{"error": "method not allowed", "allowed": ["GET", "POST"]}`) but that requires the `crate::response` module, a `JsonBody` trait, and a serde dep on the router — all out of scope. The Allow header alone is what RFC 9110 §15.5.6 mandates; clients that want to act on the error machine-readably already use the header.

Files changed:
- jolt-core/src/router.rs — `Router::call` now collects path-match-method-miss entries during the registry walk and surfaces 405 (with `Allow` header) when no verb matched but the path did. Added `method_not_allowed(allowed: &[Method]) -> Response` helper. Updated module docstring's phase07 ladder: 036 is now landed, 037 is current, with explicit RFC 9110 §15.5.6 citation for the 405 contract.
- jolt-core/src/tests.rs — replaced `method_mismatch_on_registered_path_returns_404` with `method_mismatch_on_registered_path_returns_405`. Added `method_mismatch_returns_405_with_allow_header_listing_registered_method` (single-method Allow value), `method_mismatch_returns_405_with_allow_listing_all_registered_methods` (multi-method Allow value, deterministic order), `unknown_path_returns_404_not_405_even_when_registry_is_populated` (path-discrimination contract + asserts no Allow header on 404), and `unparseable_http_verb_returns_404_even_for_registered_path` (CONNECT pinned to 404). All four new tests live under `mod registry_dispatch`.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-037 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- Phase07 is now closed (033..037 all landed). Phase08 (JOLT-RS-038, `proc_macro_attribute` for `#[endpoint(path)]`) is the next architectural item and the next phase entry. Step text is "parse the path argument from attribute tokens." This is the start of macro work — a new `jolt-macros` crate likely already exists (need to check); if not, the 038 work includes scaffolding it. Verification is "Unit test: `#[endpoint("/api/test")]` extracts path = "/api/test"."
- The `Inner::Axum` retirement question (deferred from 035, 036, and now 037): still open. The 3 prior 033 tests + `service_call_forwards_to_inner_axum_router_for_unmatched_paths` ride on `Inner::Axum`. Retiring it now would require rewriting them around registry-based fixtures and dropping the axum-router compat path. Recommend creating a dedicated PRD item ("retire `Inner::Axum`, collapse Router to Arc<EndpointRegistry>") rather than absorbing it into a phase07 item — phase07 is closed, and this is a cleanup tied to the inner type's storage shape, not a behavior change.
- The `unparseable_http_verb_returns_404` test pins the conservative behavior. If a future PRD wants RFC 9110 §15.6.2 compliance (501 Not Implemented for unrecognized methods), the migration is one line in `Router::call`'s `Method::from_str` branch + one test rewrite. Worth raising as a tracker item when phase08+ stabilizes — clients that test against compliant frameworks may notice the 404-vs-501 divergence.
- `Method::as_str` is now used in two production sites: the `from_str`/`Display` round-trip (long-standing) and the new `Allow`-header builder. If a third site appears (e.g. a logging middleware that wants the canonical name), the function stays as-is. No refactor needed.
- The `mod registry_dispatch` test file now has 16 tests. The 036 progress note flagged ~15 as the threshold for splitting by concern (constructor / dispatch / short-circuit). With the 037 additions sitting in the same flat module, the split is now a worthwhile cleanup — but it's purely organizational, not behavioral, and not in scope for any PRD item. Tag for future cleanup: split into submodules `mod basic_dispatch`, `mod method_mismatch`, `mod short_circuit`, `mod constructor`.
- Allow header order is registry-insertion order. If a future PRD wants a canonical order (e.g. RFC verb-list order: GET, HEAD, POST, PUT, DELETE, OPTIONS, PATCH), the 405 helper grows ~5 lines (sort by a `verb_canonical_order(Method) -> u8` mapping). Not yet justified.
- JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict test) is still the only phase05 holdout. Same ~10-line shape from prior progress notes.
- JOLT-RS-032 (endpoint-registry test bundle): same wait — duplicate-path detection design choice + path-param extraction Request-field decision both still open. With phase07 closed, this is the natural next polish item to pick up before phase08; the path-param extraction question has a new constraint though: phase08's `#[endpoint("/users/:id")]` will need to surface params somewhere, so the Request-field decision should likely be made FIRST inside phase08's PRD items rather than as a 032 prerequisite.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-038: #[endpoint(path)] attribute path parsing

PRD item: JOLT-RS-038 (priority 38, phase08-endpoint-macro-parsing) — implement `#[proc_macro_attribute] pub fn endpoint(attr, item)` that parses the path string literal from the attribute tokens. Opens phase08.

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 038 is the architectural opener for phase08 — it locks in the parser shape that JOLT-RS-039 (method scan), 040 (signature validation), and 041 (handler-match codegen) all build on. Landing it now means downstream items have a stable `parse_endpoint_attr` helper to extend rather than each invent its own path parser. JOLT-RS-027/032 remain pure-polish/test-bundle items with no upstream dependencies (and 037's progress notes already flagged that the path-param Request-field decision belongs INSIDE phase08, not as a 032 prerequisite).

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-macros` → clean in 0.07s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-macros` → 7/7 passed (extracts simple/root/path-param paths; rejects empty / integer / bare-ident / trailing-tokens).
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.31s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

The PRD-mandated verification ("Unit test: `#[endpoint("/api/test")]` extracts path = "/api/test"") is the `extracts_simple_path` test in `endpoint::tests`.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..037 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool. (The repo has no `package.json`, no `server/` directory.)

Key decisions:
- **Parsing extracted into a non-proc-macro helper (`endpoint::parse_endpoint_attr`).** Proc-macro entry points (`#[proc_macro_attribute]` fns) cannot be invoked outside the compiler — they take/return the `proc_macro::TokenStream` type, which is only valid inside a proc-macro context. To make the path-extraction logic unit-testable, the parsing layer takes a `proc_macro2::TokenStream` (the test-friendly mirror crate that proc_macro2 provides) and lives in a sibling `endpoint.rs` module. The proc-macro entry point in `lib.rs` is a thin shim: convert `proc_macro::TokenStream` → `proc_macro2::TokenStream`, call the helper, convert back. This is the standard pattern (e.g. dtolnay's `paste`, `serde_derive`, `thiserror` all split this way) and is what JOLT-RS-039+ will extend.
- **`syn::parse2::<LitStr>(tokens)` is the parser.** When you write `#[endpoint("/api/test")]`, the `attr` TokenStream the compiler hands the proc-macro contains exactly the tokens between the parens — `"/api/test"`. So parsing as `syn::LitStr` is the minimal correct shape: it accepts a single string literal and rejects everything else (integers, bare idents, multi-arg lists like `"/foo", "extra"`) with a built-in span-pointing error. Rolling our own parser (e.g. peeking a TokenTree and matching on `Literal::String`) would re-implement what `syn` already does and lose the diagnostic quality. If JOLT-RS-039 wants additional optional kwargs like `#[endpoint("/api/test", auth = "jwt")]`, the parser grows into `Punctuated<NestedMeta, Token![,]>` or a custom `Parse` impl — but that's strictly out of scope for 038's "parse the path argument from attribute tokens" step.
- **Errors surface via `to_compile_error()` AND keep the original item.** When parsing fails, the macro emits `compile_error!(...)` tokens APPENDED to the original (unmodified) item. Two reasons: (a) without re-emitting the item, every site downstream that names the struct/impl gets a confusing "use of undeclared type" cascade on top of the real diagnostic; (b) the user's error message points at the malformed attribute argument span (via `syn::Error`'s span), which is exactly where the fix is. Rejected alternative: emit ONLY the `compile_error!` (drop the item), which is the dtolnay convention for some macros — but for an attribute on an impl block where the inner methods may be called from elsewhere in the user's crate, dropping the impl turns one error into many.
- **Kept `jolt_placeholder` and `JoltPlaceholder` placeholders.** They were originally described as "Future PRD items will expand this." 038 is one such future item, but it adds a NEW symbol (`endpoint`) rather than replacing `jolt_placeholder` (since `jolt_placeholder` was a no-op stub on `ItemFn` and `endpoint` will eventually run on impl blocks — different shape). Removing the placeholders now would be cleanup unrelated to 038; "Keep the change small and focused" wins. They'll naturally disappear when phase11 (`AutoMiddleware` derive) and phase15 (`TsExport` derive) replace `JoltPlaceholder`, and a future cleanup item can drop the dead `jolt_placeholder` attribute.
- **`#[allow(dead_code)]` on `EndpointAttr.path` is deliberate, not a hack.** This iteration only PARSES — it doesn't read the parsed path back out (since codegen lands in JOLT-RS-041). Without the allow, a `dead_code` warning fires on the production build (cfg(test) reads it via the test assertion, but not the proc-macro entry point). The two alternatives — (a) consume the field in the entry point with `_ = parsed.path` to silence it, or (b) skip the struct and have `parse_endpoint_attr` return `LitStr` directly — both create more cleanup work for JOLT-RS-039+ when the struct grows additional fields (method_attrs, optional kwargs). The allow with a comment naming the next-iteration consumer is the lowest-friction path.
- **Test surface deliberately broad: 3 happy-path cases + 4 rejection cases.** The PRD verification step asks for exactly one happy-path test (`/api/test`), but the cost of adding the surrounding 6 was ~15 lines. The rationale for each rejection test: `rejects_empty_attr` pins that `#[endpoint]` (no args) is an error, not a default-to-empty-path; `rejects_integer_literal` pins that `#[endpoint(123)]` doesn't silently coerce; `rejects_bare_identifier` pins that `#[endpoint(path)]` (where `path` is a name, not a string) is rejected at parse time rather than later as "use of undeclared name `path`"; `rejects_trailing_tokens_after_path` pins that `#[endpoint("/api/test", "extra")]` errors NOW rather than silently dropping `"extra"` — load-bearing for JOLT-RS-039+ when optional kwargs land, since each kwarg addition will need to flip ONE of these tests to passing instead of needing to invent test infrastructure. The two extra happy-path tests (`extracts_root_path`, `extracts_path_with_param_placeholder`) pin the contract that the parser is path-content-agnostic — phase08's later `:param` placeholder extraction is a pre-codegen pass on the literal value, not the parser.
- **Tests live in the same file as the parser (`endpoint::tests` module), not in a top-level `tests/` directory.** Proc-macro crates can't have `tests/` integration tests that exercise the proc-macros themselves (the compiler-driver setup is non-trivial — usually requires `trybuild` or similar), but inline `#[cfg(test)]` modules CAN test pure helpers like `parse_endpoint_attr` because those don't go through the compiler's proc-macro machinery. Keeping them inline keeps the parsing logic and its tests adjacent — a pattern that scales for JOLT-RS-039+'s additions.

Files changed:
- jolt-macros/src/endpoint.rs (new) — `EndpointAttr` struct (just `path: LitStr` for now, with `#[allow(dead_code)]` until JOLT-RS-041 reads it for codegen), `parse_endpoint_attr(tokens) -> syn::Result<EndpointAttr>` helper, and 7 unit tests under `mod tests`. Module docstring lists the phase08 ladder (038 → 041).
- jolt-macros/src/lib.rs — added `mod endpoint;`, added `#[proc_macro_attribute] pub fn endpoint(attr, item) -> TokenStream` that converts to `proc_macro2::TokenStream`, calls `parse_endpoint_attr`, and either re-emits the original item (success) or emits the original item plus a `compile_error!` (failure). Kept `jolt_placeholder` / `JoltPlaceholder` placeholders untouched.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-038 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-039 (priority 39, phase08): "Scan the impl block for methods annotated with #[get], #[post], #[put], #[patch], #[delete]. Collect method sigs (name, …)." This is where the macro starts looking at `item` (currently passed through unchanged). The shape: parse `item` as `syn::ItemImpl`, walk `impl.items`, filter to `ImplItem::Fn`, collect those with one of the five attributes. Recommend: extract a `endpoint::scan_methods(item: &ItemImpl) -> syn::Result<Vec<DiscoveredMethod>>` helper that mirrors `parse_endpoint_attr`'s shape so the test surface stays uniform. Open question for 039: are `#[get]`/`#[post]`/etc. registered as separate proc-macro attributes (so they exist in scope independently of `#[endpoint]`) or are they "magic markers" that only `#[endpoint]` recognizes? Spec_rust.md doesn't say. The Zig version inspects them at comptime via reflection; the closest Rust idiom is "magic markers" (the `#[endpoint]` macro consumes them and they don't need to be registered as their own proc-macros). Recommend going with magic-markers for simplicity — it's what `tokio::main` and `axum::debug_handler` do for the `#[handler]`-style attributes they recognize.
- JOLT-RS-040 (priority 40, phase08): Validate that each discovered method has `&self` as the first arg and returns `Result<Response<T>, E>` or `Response<T>`. This is the first iteration that depends on `crate::response::Response` type machinery in jolt-core, which means jolt-macros may need to either reference `jolt_core::response::Response` by name (string match in syn) or rely on type-check-time errors from the user's code. The Zig version was content with comptime reflection on the return type; Rust syn-level inspection is name-based. Pin this as a name-based check (look for `Result<` and `Response<` in the type tokens) for now, with a note that strict typing comes from rustc's regular type-check pass on the generated code.
- JOLT-RS-041 (priority 41, phase08): Generate the (Method, path) → handler match. This is where `EndpointAttr.path` gets read for the first time — at that point the `#[allow(dead_code)]` comes off `EndpointAttr.path`.
- The `endpoint` macro currently does not register the path with anything (it's a parse-and-pass-through). JOLT-RS-042/044 wire up the inventory-based registration. Until then, applying `#[endpoint("/path")]` to an impl block is a no-op — but it's a no-op that VALIDATES the path is a string literal, which catches the most common typo class up-front.
- JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict test) and JOLT-RS-032 (endpoint-registry test bundle) are still the two phase05/phase06 holdouts. Same status as prior entries.
- The `proc_macro2::TokenStream` ↔ `proc_macro::TokenStream` conversion in the `endpoint` entry point uses `.into()`. If/when a future PRD wants pretty-printed error messages with custom spans (beyond what `syn::Error::to_compile_error()` gives), the entry point grows ~3 lines — but the conversion shape stays the same.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-039: scan impl block for #[get]/#[post]/etc. verb attributes

PRD item: JOLT-RS-039 (priority 39, phase08-endpoint-macro-parsing) — scan the impl block for methods annotated with `#[get]`, `#[post]`, `#[put]`, `#[patch]`, `#[delete]`; collect method sigs (name, args, return type).

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 039 is the architectural follow-up to 038's `parse_endpoint_attr` and the precondition for 040 (signature validation) and 041 (handler-match codegen). Landing it now means 040 and 041 build on a stable `scan_methods` shape rather than each inventing a new method-discovery walker. JOLT-RS-027/032 remain pure-polish/test-bundle items with no upstream dependencies. (038's progress notes explicitly identified 039 as the next architectural item.)

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-macros` → clean in 0.51s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-macros` → 15/15 passed (the 7 prior 038 tests + 8 new 039 tests covering the PRD-mandated single-GET case + four supporting discoverability tests + three rejection/ignore tests).
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.31s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

The PRD-mandated verification ("Unit test: impl block with #[get] fn hello(...) → found method 'hello' tagged as GET") is the `discovers_single_get_method` test in `endpoint::tests`.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..038 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool. The repo has no `package.json` and no `server/` directory.

Key decisions:
- **Magic-marker semantics for verb attributes (NOT separate `#[proc_macro_attribute]` registrations).** Per 038's open question, picked the magic-marker approach: `#[get]`/`#[post]`/`#[put]`/`#[patch]`/`#[delete]` are recognized only by `#[endpoint]`'s scanner; they are NOT registered as their own proc-macro attributes in jolt-macros's lib.rs. Rationale: (a) registering five proc-macro attributes that all do nothing is noise — they'd need stub `#[proc_macro_attribute] pub fn get(...) -> TokenStream { item }` implementations; (b) the `#[endpoint]` macro already owns the impl block and gets to decide what `#[get]` means inside it, the same way `tokio::main` and `axum::debug_handler` recognize sub-attributes without registering them as macros; (c) JOLT-RS-041 will need to STRIP the verb attributes when re-emitting the impl (otherwise rustc errors with "cannot find attribute `get`"), and it's strictly easier to strip an attribute the macro recognizes than to maintain five no-op macros. The cost is that `#[get]` is invalid OUTSIDE an `#[endpoint]`-decorated impl, but that's exactly the desired UX — a stray `#[get]` on a free function should error rather than silently no-op.
- **Verb matcher is bare-attribute-only: `#[get]`, NOT `#[get("/path")]` or `#[axum::get]`.** The matcher checks both `attr.meta` is `Meta::Path(_)` (no parens, no `=`) AND `attr.path().get_ident()` is single-segment. Rejected the looser `attr.path().get_ident()`-only check because it would match `#[get("/with-path")]` (axum's route-attribute shape) and steal it from a user who imported `axum::get`. The narrow matcher mirrors how rustfmt and clippy treat magic-marker attributes — only the canonical bare form is recognized. Pinned by `ignores_path_style_and_argful_verb_attributes` which exercises both the multi-segment `#[axum::get]` rejection AND the argful `#[get("/with-path")]` rejection in the same test, while the bare `#[get]` in the same impl IS captured.
- **Multi-verb attribute on a single method is a parse error, NOT a silent first-wins.** A method tagged with both `#[get]` and `#[post]` is malformed — supporting "this handler responds to either verb" is a different feature than 039's scope. Erroring at parse-time surfaces the bug at the user's site (the second verb-attribute span carries the diagnostic) rather than later when the registry sees a duplicated handler. The error message names all five recognized verbs so the user can pick one. Pinned by `rejects_method_with_two_verb_attributes`. If a future PRD wants multi-verb handlers, this check relaxes into a `Vec<HttpMethod>` per `DiscoveredMethod` — a clean migration with no contract breakage on the single-verb path.
- **`HttpMethod` enum lives in jolt-macros, not jolt-core.** Considered importing `jolt_core::Method` directly so the macro emits the same enum it'll route to. Rejected because (a) jolt-core depends on jolt-macros at the workspace level once macros are re-exported through jolt-core's prelude (the planned shape per spec_rust.md), creating a cycle; (b) proc-macro crates can only depend on other proc-macro / build-time crates without a runtime/compile-time split, and pulling jolt-core into jolt-macros's `[dependencies]` would build all of axum + tokio at proc-macro time. The workaround is a 5-variant local mirror; codegen in JOLT-RS-041 will emit `::jolt_core::Method::Get` etc. as a quoted path rather than referencing the enum value directly. Documented this in `HttpMethod`'s rustdoc + flagged the `as_jolt_core_variant_ident` helper as a 041 add.
- **`DiscoveredMethod.sig` is an owned `Signature` clone, not a borrow.** Considered `&'a Signature` so we don't pay the clone cost. Rejected because (a) `Signature` clones are cheap (mostly Vec<Box<...>> and String moves — no syntax-tree deep-walks since each field is already a leaf), (b) callers in JOLT-RS-040 and 041 will want to inspect the signature without holding a borrow on the input `ItemImpl` (e.g. building a `Vec<DiscoveredMethod>` and then walking it after the input goes out of scope), and (c) the `Vec<DiscoveredMethod>` return type forces ownership anyway — owned signatures inside force the rest of the struct to be owned, which is what callers want regardless. The lifetime-free `DiscoveredMethod` is also easier to thread through downstream codegen helpers.
- **Helper methods (no verb attribute) are SKIPPED, not errored.** An endpoint impl can legitimately mix handler methods with helper methods (`fn validate(...)`, `fn db_pool(...)`, etc.). Erroring on helpers would force users to pull every helper into a free function or a separate impl block, which is a UX regression from the Zig version's design. Pinned by `skips_methods_without_verb_attribute` which has both a bare `fn helper(&self)` and an `#[inline] fn other_helper(...)` (the `#[inline]` attribute is NOT a verb attribute and must not trigger any rejection logic). Non-fn impl items (consts, type aliases) are similarly ignored — pinned by `ignores_non_fn_impl_items`. The `let ImplItem::Fn(method_fn) = impl_item else { continue; };` shape uses let-else which keeps the loop body flat.
- **`#[allow(dead_code)]` on `HttpMethod::from_attr_name`, `DiscoveredMethod` (struct + fields), `scan_methods`, and `verb_from_attr`.** Same pattern as 038's `EndpointAttr.path`: this iteration adds the parsing surface, but the proc-macro entry point in `lib.rs` does NOT call `scan_methods` yet (that wires in via 040's signature validation step). Without the allows, a `dead_code` warning fires on the production build (cfg(test) reads them via assertions but the proc-macro entry point doesn't). Each allow names the next-iteration consumer in a comment so removal is mechanical when 040/041 land.
- **`scan_methods` returns `Vec<DiscoveredMethod>` in source order (no sort).** The order of methods in an impl block is part of the source's structure; preserving it makes generated code deterministic and matches what a reader would expect from "scan top to bottom." If JOLT-RS-041's match-arm codegen wants a specific order (e.g. specific-paths-before-wildcards, mirroring router.rs's longest-path-first sort), it'll sort then. The scanner's job is discovery, not ordering.
- **Test surface: 1 PRD-mandated + 7 supporting (8 new total).** The PRD asks for one happy-path test (`#[get] fn hello(...)` → found tagged GET). The 7 supporting tests pin: (a) one-method-per-verb covers all 5 verbs (`discovers_one_method_per_verb`), (b) helper methods are skipped (`skips_methods_without_verb_attribute`), (c) non-fn impl items are ignored (`ignores_non_fn_impl_items`), (d) empty impl returns empty vec (`empty_impl_returns_empty_vec` — surfaces a regression that defaulted to a 1-element vec or panicked on empty input), (e) signature is captured intact for 040 to inspect (`captures_signature_inputs_and_output` — checks input arity and that `ReturnType` is `Type(_, _)` not `Default`), (f) multi-verb is an error (`rejects_method_with_two_verb_attributes`), (g) path-style and argful attributes are not stolen (`ignores_path_style_and_argful_verb_attributes`). The cost was ~120 lines of test code; the rationale for breadth is the same as 038 — each test pins one independently-observable contract that JOLT-RS-040+ will rely on.
- **Test fixtures use `syn::parse_str::<ItemImpl>(...)` via a `parse_impl(src: &str)` helper.** Considered building `ItemImpl` values via `quote! { ... }` + `parse2`. Rejected because raw-string source is more readable in tests (the test reader sees the literal Rust the user would write), and `parse_str` is slightly more direct than `quote!` + `parse2` for fixed inputs. The helper hides the `.expect("test input parses as ItemImpl")` so individual tests stay focused on assertions.

Files changed:
- jolt-macros/src/endpoint.rs — added `HttpMethod` enum (`Get`/`Post`/`Put`/`Patch`/`Delete`) with `from_attr_name(&str) -> Option<Self>`; added `DiscoveredMethod { http_method, sig }` struct; added `scan_methods(&ItemImpl) -> syn::Result<Vec<DiscoveredMethod>>` and the private `verb_from_attr(&Attribute) -> Option<HttpMethod>` helper; updated module docstring to mark 038 landed and 039 current with explicit note that verb attributes are magic-marker (recognized only inside `#[endpoint]`-decorated impls). Added 8 new unit tests under `mod endpoint::tests` plus a `parse_impl` helper.
- prd.json — JOLT-RS-039 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- JOLT-RS-040 (priority 40, phase08): "Validate each method signature: first arg must be `&self`, must return `Result<Response<T>, E>` or `Response<T>`. Error on mismatch with clear span." Now has a `Vec<DiscoveredMethod>` to walk. The first-arg check reads `sig.inputs.first()`, expects `FnArg::Receiver(r)` with `r.reference.is_some()` and `r.mutability.is_none()`. The return-type check is the harder one because syn-level type inspection is name-based: matching "any type whose path's last segment is `Response` OR `Result` whose first generic arg's last segment is `Response`" is the pragmatic shape. Strict typing comes from rustc on the generated code; the macro check just catches the obvious typos (return `()`, return `String`) at parse time. Recommend: extract a `endpoint::validate_signature(&Signature) -> syn::Result<()>` helper that mirrors `parse_endpoint_attr`/`scan_methods`'s shape, and call it from `scan_methods` so the discovered list only contains validated methods. Alternative: keep validation as a separate pass `validate_methods(&[DiscoveredMethod]) -> syn::Result<()>` so 039's pure-discovery contract stays clean. Slight preference for the second since `scan_methods`'s test surface is already broad and adding validation would force every test fixture to use a valid signature.
- JOLT-RS-041 (priority 41, phase08): Generate the (Method, path) → handler match. This is where `EndpointAttr.path` AND the `Vec<DiscoveredMethod>` finally meet. The match arm shape will likely be `(jolt_core::Method::Get, "/api/test") => Self::hello`; the magic-marker verb attribute MUST be stripped from the re-emitted impl to avoid "cannot find attribute `get`" from rustc. Recommend: extract a `endpoint::strip_verb_attrs(&mut ItemImpl)` helper that walks `item.items` and removes any `Attribute` matching `verb_from_attr`. The magic-marker semantics decided in 039 make this trivial.
- The `endpoint` macro entry point in lib.rs still does NOT consume `scan_methods` this iteration. It will start consuming it in 040 (when validation joins parsing) and become the codegen driver in 041. The current "validates path is a string literal, re-emits item" no-op behavior is unchanged.
- The single-verb-per-method check could be relaxed in a future PRD to support `#[get] #[head] fn ...` for handlers that respond to both verbs identically. The `Vec<HttpMethod>` shape is the natural migration. Not currently justified by spec_rust.md.
- `HttpMethod` is currently a 5-variant enum without `Head` or `Options`. Rationale: jolt-core's `Method` enum has all 7, but only 5 are user-routable; `Head` and `Options` are framework-handled (Allow header / auto-OPTIONS). If a future PRD wants user-defined HEAD or OPTIONS handlers, this enum grows and `from_attr_name` adds the corresponding match arms.
- JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict test) and JOLT-RS-032 (endpoint-registry test bundle) are still the two phase05/phase06 holdouts. Same status as prior entries.
- The `mod endpoint::tests` module now has 15 tests. Still flat (no submodule split). At ~25 the same split-by-concern advice from 037's progress note applies: `mod attr_parsing` (extracts/rejects) + `mod method_scanning` (discovery) + `mod magic_marker` (verb-matcher edge cases). Not yet justified.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-040: validate handler signature (`&self` + `Response<T>` / `Result<Response<T>, E>`)

PRD item: JOLT-RS-040 (priority 40, phase08-endpoint-macro-parsing) — validate each method signature: first arg must be `&self`, return type must be `Response<T>` or `Result<Response<T>, E>`. Error on mismatch with clear span.

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 040 is the next phase08 architectural item — it locks in the validation contract that JOLT-RS-041's match-arm codegen will assume (every signature in the discovered list is well-formed; the codegen pass can emit `Self::hello` without re-checking the receiver shape) and that the eventual phase11 auto-middleware codegen will rely on (extra args after `&self` may be present and must be processed). Landing it now also closes the 038→040 parsing surface so 041 can focus purely on emission. JOLT-RS-027/032 remain pure-polish/test-bundle items with no upstream dependencies.

Verification:
- `cargo check -p jolt-macros` → clean in 0.60s.
- `cargo test -p jolt-macros` → 31/31 passed (15 prior 038/039 tests + 16 new 040 tests covering 4 happy-path shapes + 6 receiver rejections + 5 return-type rejections + 1 multi-method walker test).
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean in 0.31s; no regressions in any sibling crate.

The PRD-mandated verification ("Unit test: method with wrong signature → compile error with descriptive message") is satisfied by every `rejects_*` test — each asserts `validate_signature` returns `Err` and that the diagnostic mentions the offending shape (`&self` or `Response<T>`) so users see what to fix. `syn::Error` flows into `compile_error!` tokens at the proc-macro layer (already wired in lib.rs's existing `endpoint` entry point for `parse_endpoint_attr`).

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..039 — auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply to this Rust workspace; cargo is the verification tool. (No `package.json`, no `server/` directory.)

Key decisions:
- **`validate_methods` is a separate pass, NOT folded into `scan_methods`.** Per 039's progress notes, two designs were on the table: (a) call `validate_signature` from inside `scan_methods` so the returned list is pre-validated, or (b) keep `scan_methods` as pure discovery and run `validate_methods` after. Picked (b) because (i) 039's existing test fixtures use signatures that don't satisfy 040's validation (e.g. `fn hello(&self) {}` returns `()`, not `Response<T>`), and folding validation into `scan_methods` would force every existing test to grow a return-type annotation just to keep compiling; (ii) the two passes have orthogonal concerns — discovery is name-pattern matching against attributes, validation is shape-checking against the signature — and keeping them separable means a future caller that wants raw discovery (say, for a tool that lists all `#[endpoint]`-tagged methods regardless of signature health) can call `scan_methods` without paying the validation cost; (iii) the call sites in 041+ will naturally chain `scan_methods(...)?` then `validate_methods(...)?` — same one-line discipline as folding-in, with strictly more flexibility. Documented this choice in `validate_methods`'s rustdoc.
- **Validation is name-only on the LAST PATH SEGMENT.** A return type is "valid" iff its last path segment's identifier is `Response` (1-arg case) or `Result` whose first generic arg has last segment `Response` (2-arg case). This deliberately accepts `Response<T>`, `crate::Response<T>`, `jolt_core::Response<T>`, `jolt_core::response::Response<T>`, AND bare `Response` (no generic args). Pinned by `accepts_qualified_response_path`. The rationale: the macro is a syn-level pre-flight check — its job is to catch obvious typos (`String`, `i32`, `()`) at expansion time so the user gets a span-pointing diagnostic instead of a confusing rustc error from generated code that names a non-existent handler. Strict identity (must literally be `jolt_core::response::Response`) is enforced by rustc on the generated dispatch code, which is the right gate for type identity. The 039 progress notes flagged this exact tradeoff: "Strict typing comes from rustc on the generated code; the macro check just catches the obvious typos."
- **Receiver rules: `&self` only — `&mut self`, owned `self`, and typed receivers are ALL rejected.** Each rejection has its own diagnostic message so users see exactly what's wrong and why. The "why" lines matter: (a) `&self` is required because handlers run on a shared `&Endpoint` (the registry holds `Box<dyn Endpoint + Send + Sync>` per JOLT-RS-029, so handlers must be callable through a shared reference); (b) `&mut self` would force exclusive access per call, defeating the registry's `Arc`-shared dispatch and breaking concurrency; (c) owned `self` would consume the endpoint each call, which is incoherent with the registry storing one instance per route; (d) typed receivers (`self: Box<Self>`, `self: Pin<&Self>`) are not standard handler shapes and the registry doesn't dispatch through them. Each rejection's error message names the specific anti-pattern it catches so the user can fix the right thing. Pinned by `rejects_mut_self_receiver`, `rejects_owned_self_receiver`, `rejects_typed_receiver`.
- **`rejects_unit_return_type` pins the `Type::Tuple`-not-`Type::Path` branch.** The `last_path_segment` helper returns `None` for any non-`Type::Path` (tuples, references, slices, fn pointers, ...). Without this test, a regression that special-cased `()` (e.g. `if matches!(ty, Type::Tuple(_))` short-circuiting to `Ok`) would silently allow `fn handler(&self) -> ()`, which is the most common typo for a handler that forgot to add a return type. The unit case is the canonical Type::Tuple example; one test covers the whole class.
- **`rejects_bare_result_without_type_args` pins a panic-class regression.** syn parses `Result` (no `<...>`) as a Type::Path with `PathArguments::None` — completely valid syntactically. The validator's `Result` branch must check `args` is `AngleBracketed(_)` BEFORE indexing into `.first()`, or it panics. The test forces the well-formed `PathArguments::AngleBracketed` check to stay in place. Without it, a refactor that flattened the match could regress to `args.first()` on a `None`-typed PathArguments and panic at compile time of the user's code — terrible UX. (`Result` with no generics is invalid Rust at the type level, so rustc catches it later, but the macro must surface a clean diagnostic, not crash.)
- **`accepts_extra_args_after_self` pins the auto-middleware (phase11) compatibility.** Phase11's `#[derive(AutoMiddleware)]` will inject body / query / req fields that surface as additional fn args after `&self`. The validator MUST NOT reject `fn handler(&self, body: T, query: Q) -> Response<U>`. A regression that checked `sig.inputs.len() == 1` (i.e. `&self` only) would compile and pass the basic accept test but break every auto-middleware handler. Pinning the multi-arg shape now means that contract is locked before phase11 starts.
- **`validate_methods` stops at the first error, does NOT collect all errors.** Considered accumulating errors across all methods so users see every problem at once.
