- **Module split: `jolt-macros/src/auto_middleware.rs` mirrors `endpoint.rs`'s structure.** Parsing + expansion logic lives in the module; `lib.rs` is a 3-line proc-macro entry-point shim that delegates to `expand_auto_middleware`. Same pattern as `endpoint::expand_endpoint`. Considered putting it inside `endpoint.rs` since both relate to phase08-09's macro pipeline — rejected because (a) `endpoint.rs` is already 1535 lines and the test surface is at 59 tests, well past the ~25 split-by-concern threshold flagged in 040-044's progress notes; (b) `#[derive(AutoMiddleware)]` is a derive (operates on a struct decl), `#[endpoint]` is an attribute (operates on an impl block) — they share no helpers and have different parse-input types (`DeriveInput` vs `ItemImpl`). A shared `parse_struct_attrs` helper might emerge later (when 050 adds `#[cors]` detection on the struct), but until then the modules are properly separate.
- **Accept named-fields struct + unit struct; reject tuple struct, enum, and union.** Named-fields: the canonical shape per the spec ("auto-applies body parsing if `body: T` field exists, query parsing if `query_params` field exists, CORS if `#[cors]` attribute present"). Unit struct: accepted as a no-field passthrough — the layer codegen in 051+ still emits the `tower::Layer` impl, just with no body/query/req injection. A unit middleware is useful for declaring scope-only marker types (e.g. a struct that exists only to compose user-defined middleware fns). Tuple struct: rejected. Field-kind detection in 047-049 keys on field NAMES (`body`, `query_params`, `req`); positional fields can't carry that meaning. Accepting them would force a separate kind-detection rule that doesn't compose with named-field structs — and there's no demand for tuple-shaped middlewares in the spec. Enum/union: rejected with a span pointing at the offending keyword. Diagnostics enumerate the constraint in plain English so users see one targeted error rather than a downstream "use of undeclared const __JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT".
- **Parsed shape: `AutoMiddlewareInput { ident, fields: Vec<AutoMiddlewareField> }` with `AutoMiddlewareField { ident, ty }`.** Captures per-field metadata verbatim from `syn::Field`. Three considered shapes: (a) `Vec<(Ident, Type)>` — minimal but loses room to extend; (b) `Vec<AutoMiddlewareField { ident, ty }>` — current choice, opens room for kind classification; (c) `Vec<AutoMiddlewareField { ident, ty, kind: FieldKind }>` — premature, since 046's job is just parsing, not classification. Picked (b) so that 047-049 can extend the struct with `kind: FieldKind` without changing 046's parse-time storage shape (the rendered TokenStream, the unit-test assertions, or the integration-test contract). The struct derives `Debug + Clone` matching the existing pattern on `endpoint::DiscoveredMethod`.
- **Emit a single hidden const `__JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT: usize` rather than a struct constant or trait impl.** Three alternatives: (a) hidden marker fn (mirrors `JoltPlaceholder` derive's `__jolt_placeholder()`) — works but is harder to assert against in the integration test (you'd assert the fn exists by calling it); (b) hidden trait impl `impl __JoltAutoMiddleware for Struct` with a `FIELD_COUNT` associated const — adds a trait that 047+ would have to keep in sync; (c) the const (current choice) — minimal, stable, asserts cleanly, and disappears cleanly when 051+ replaces it with the real `tower::Layer` impl. The double-underscore prefix follows Rust's compiler-internal-ident convention so user struct fields named `_field_count` or `field_count` won't collide. `#[doc(hidden)]` keeps it out of `cargo doc` output. `#[automatically_derived]` on the impl block makes the diagnostic message clearer if a future bug emits the const but with a wrong type ("`MyStruct::__JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT` was automatically derived"). The `pub` visibility is required so the integration test in `jolt-core/tests/` can reach the const from a different module.
- **The const carries the FIELD COUNT, not the field idents/types.** Considered emitting `pub const __JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_NAMES: [&'static str; N] = [...]` so the test could assert names. Rejected because (a) the field count is sufficient parse-witness for 046's verification — the unit tests in `mod auto_middleware::tests` assert per-field idents and types directly on `AutoMiddlewareInput`; (b) emitting a name array commits the derive to a public surface that 051+ may not want to maintain (when the marker const goes away, what replaces it?); (c) integration tests should test through public APIs, not through macro-internal observables — and any name-based assertion at the test level would be redundant with the layer-codegen tests in 051+.
- **Parse failure → single `compile_error!` token, no partial codegen.** Mirrors the same pattern as `endpoint::expand_endpoint`. The user sees one underlined error rather than a cascade of "use of undeclared const __JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT" from later code that names the user's struct. The integration test does NOT cover parse-failure cases (those are unit-tested in the macro crate); a `compile_fail` doc-test or `trybuild` setup would be the right place to test this through cargo, but neither is set up in this repo, and the unit tests already cover the failure-mode tokenization.
- **Test surface: 10 new unit tests in `mod auto_middleware::tests` + 2 new integration tests = 12 new tests for 046.** Unit tests pin: parse-time success on unit/single-named-field/various-types structs; parse-time rejection on enum/union/tuple-struct with diagnostic-message content checks; expand-time emission of the marker const + automatically_derived attr; expand-time emission of zero count for unit struct; expand-time compile_error on enum + tuple-struct (no marker emission). Integration tests pin: derive compiles on UnitMiddleware (zero fields) AND on MixedMiddleware (six fields spanning the type families 047-049 will key on); the `__JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT` const has the expected values.

Files changed:
- `jolt-macros/src/auto_middleware.rs` (new) — module hosting `parse_auto_middleware_input`, `parse_struct_fields`, `expand_auto_middleware`, `AutoMiddlewareInput`, `AutoMiddlewareField`. 10 unit tests under `mod tests` covering the parse + expand surfaces.
- `jolt-macros/src/lib.rs` — added `mod auto_middleware;`. Added `#[proc_macro_derive(AutoMiddleware)] pub fn auto_middleware_derive` proc-macro entry point that delegates to `auto_middleware::expand_auto_middleware`. Added rustdoc enumerating phase10's 046-053 ladder.
- `jolt-core/src/lib.rs` — extended the existing `pub use jolt_macros::endpoint;` re-export to also re-export `AutoMiddleware` (`pub use jolt_macros::{endpoint, AutoMiddleware};`). Same pattern as `endpoint`: user crates `use jolt_core::AutoMiddleware;` instead of pulling jolt-macros directly.
- `jolt-core/tests/auto_middleware_derive.rs` (new) — PRD-mandated integration test. Defines `UnitMiddleware` (unit struct) and `MixedMiddleware` (six fields spanning custom DeserializeOwned-shaped, HashMap, primitive, Option-wrapped framework type). Asserts `__JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT` is 0 and 6 respectively.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-046 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- **JOLT-RS-047 (priority 47, phase10): "Detect body fields: any field typed T where T: DeserializeOwned (not Request, not QueryParams). Mark as body-candidate."** Now has stable parsed input to build on. Two design questions: (a) should body-detection be name-based (`field.ident == "body"`), type-based (any non-Request, non-QueryParams type), or BOTH? The spec ("body parsing if `body: T` field exists") leans name-based. The PRD verification ("field body: CreateUserRequest → detected as body field") confirms name-based. So 047 should match on `field.ident == "body"` and capture the type for the body-extraction codegen in 053. (b) Where does the detection result land? Recommended: extend `AutoMiddlewareField` with `pub kind: FieldKind` where `FieldKind: Body | QueryParams | Request | Other`, computed at parse-time. Or a separate `pub body_field: Option<Ident>` on `AutoMiddlewareInput`. The kind-on-field shape is more uniform; the option-on-input shape is simpler if there's only one of each kind per struct. The spec's wording ("if body field exists") implies at most one — so the Option<...> shape is fine. Decide at 047.
- **JOLT-RS-048 + 049 will compose with 047's kind-detection.** Same pattern: if 047 picks `Option<BodyField>` on `AutoMiddlewareInput`, 048 adds `Option<QueryField>`, 049 adds `Option<RequestField>`. If 047 picks `kind: FieldKind` on each field, 048 adds two new variants and 049 adds one more. Either way, the parse-time data structure carries enough info that the layer codegen in 051+ can emit the right extraction calls.
- **JOLT-RS-050 (`#[cors]` struct-level attr).** Will need a `parse_struct_attrs` helper alongside `parse_struct_fields`. The current parse function ignores `input.attrs` — 050 will add `let cors_enabled = input.attrs.iter().any(|a| a.path().is_ident("cors"));` and stash it on `AutoMiddlewareInput` as `pub cors: bool`.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test).** Still the only pre-046 holdouts. 045 is mostly satisfied by 044's existing `into_router_serves_*` tests; the auto-prompt could mark it complete on the next pass with a note pointing here. 027/032 remain pure test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies.
- **`generate_dispatch_match` still has `#[allow(dead_code)]` and is unused.** Decision deferred from 043 + 044: keep or delete. No pending consumer; 4 unit tests + ~80 LOC. If 047+ converges on a per-field-kind dispatch model in the auto-middleware layer, the helper might find a second life. Otherwise delete as part of phase09 cleanup.
- **`mod endpoint::tests` still at 59 tests; `mod auto_middleware::tests` starts at 10 tests.** With 046 landed, the macro crate's total test count is 69 (59 + 10). The endpoint-tests split-by-concern recommendation from 043/044's progress notes still stands for after 045 closes. The auto_middleware tests are clean from the start (single flat module, well below the threshold) — they'll need to split when 050 closes (probable test count: 25-30 tests covering all of 046-050's parse + expand surfaces).
- **`AutoMiddlewareInput` and `AutoMiddlewareField` are `pub(crate)`.** They're internal to jolt-macros. If a future PRD wants third-party tooling (e.g. a separate `jolt-tools` crate that introspects auto-middleware structs at compile time), the right move is a separate `jolt-macros-types` crate that hosts these types and is re-exported by both jolt-macros and the third-party crate. Out of scope for 046+; flag-worthy if the framework's surface ever grows that direction.
- **Marker-const naming `__JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT` is committed.** When 051+ replaces the const with the real `tower::Layer` impl, the const can be removed cleanly (no one outside the integration test references it). The integration test in `auto_middleware_derive.rs` will need to change at that point — its assertions become "the layer impl exists and routes correctly", not "the marker const has the right value". Flag for 051's cleanup.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-047: body-field FieldKind classification

PRD item: JOLT-RS-047 (priority 47, phase10-automiddleware-field-parsing) — "Detect body fields: any field typed T where T: DeserializeOwned (not Request, not QueryParams). Mark as body-candidate." Verification: "Unit test: field body: CreateUserRequest → detected as body field."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 047 introduces the `FieldKind` enum that 048/049/051+ extend and dispatch on. It commits to (a) name-based detection (`field.ident == "body"`) over a type-based DeserializeOwned-bound check; (b) a `kind: FieldKind` field on each `AutoMiddlewareField` over a per-input `body_field: Option<Ident>` flag; (c) name-only classification at this stage with no type-based exclusions for `Request`/`QueryParams<T>` (deferred to 048/049 if a precedence rule emerges). All three decisions are load-bearing for 048-053. 027/032/045 remain test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase10+ work.

Verification:
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 111 jolt-core unit + 8 jolt-core inventory_registration integration + 2 jolt-core auto_middleware_derive integration + 66 jolt-macros unit (was 59; +7 new tests for 047, including one for the no-body-field property on unit structs) = 187 tests pass; no regressions.
- `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`); 0 new warnings.
- The PRD-mandated "Unit test: field body: CreateUserRequest → detected as body field" is satisfied by `parses_body_field_with_custom_type_as_body_kind` in `jolt-macros/src/auto_middleware.rs`'s `mod tests`. The test parses `struct WithBody { body: CreateUserRequest }`, asserts `parsed.fields[0].kind == FieldKind::Body`, and verifies the type round-trips through tokenization (so 053's `__req.json::<CreateUserRequest>()` codegen will have the right tokens).

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..046 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory). Cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **Name-based detection (`field.ident == "body"`), not type-based (T: DeserializeOwned exclusion).** The PRD description text ("any field typed T where T: DeserializeOwned (not Request, not QueryParams)") and the verification text ("field body: CreateUserRequest → detected as body field") are inconsistent — the description is type-based, the verification is name-based. The spec doc (`spec_rust.md` line 39) resolves the ambiguity: "auto-applies body parsing if `body: T` field exists" — explicitly name-based. Picked name-based for three reasons: (a) proc-macros have no access to trait-bound resolution at expand time, so a literal "T: DeserializeOwned" check is impossible without compile-fail tests; (b) the spec's wording "if `body: T` field exists" treats `body` as a reserved field name with framework-meaning, which matches how 048's `query_params` and 049's `req` work; (c) the inconsistent PRD prose can be reconciled as "the field is body-candidate by name; if T isn't actually DeserializeOwned, the body-extraction codegen in 053 will fail to compile with a clear trait-bound error at the user's struct site". The name-based rule defers the trait-bound check to where it's most natural (rustc on the generated `__req.json::<T>()` call).
- **`kind: FieldKind` per field, not `body_field: Option<Ident>` on the input.** The 046 progress notes flagged this as the open question for 047. Two shapes considered: (a) per-field `kind` enum (current choice), (b) per-input `Option<Ident>` flag for each detected role. Picked (a) because: the layer codegen in 053 will iterate fields once and emit per-field extraction calls — `parsed.fields.iter().filter(|f| f.kind == Body)` is a uniform shape; with separate Option<Ident> flags, codegen would need a hash-lookup or O(N) re-scan to find the field's *type* (which lives on `AutoMiddlewareField`), introducing unnecessary indirection. The kind-on-field shape also extends cleanly: 048 adds `QueryParams`, 049 adds `Request`, 050's struct-level `#[cors]` flag goes on `AutoMiddlewareInput` (where it belongs — it's a struct property, not a field property). The progress note's "Either way, the parse-time data structure carries enough info" is right; (a) is simpler to consume.
- **`FieldKind::Other` as the catch-all for non-`body` fields.** Considered three alternatives: (a) `Option<FieldKind>` where `None` means "no kind yet" — rejected because every field IS classified, just possibly as a passthrough; (b) `FieldKind::Unclassified` with the implication 048/049 will narrow it later — rejected because "Unclassified" implies a temporary state, but `Other` correctly conveys "no framework-special meaning, treat as Default::default() per request"; (c) `FieldKind::Other` (current) — clear, terminal, and correct for the long term: even after phase10 closes with all the kind variants in place, a user-defined field that isn't `body`/`query_params`/`req` and doesn't match any framework type WILL be `Other`, and codegen will treat it as `Default::default()`. The progress note in the enum's rustdoc spells this out so 048/049/053 don't need to revisit it.
- **Type captured verbatim from `syn::Field.ty` regardless of kind.** Consistent with 046's existing behavior. The reason matters for codegen in 053: the body-extraction call is `__req.json::<#ty>()`, where `#ty` is spliced from the user's source. If a user writes `body: crate::api::CreateUser`, the codegen needs the FULL path token, not a stripped ident. The test `parses_body_field_with_custom_type_as_body_kind` round-trips the type through `quote!(#ty).to_string()` to pin this — a regression that called `field.ty.last().ident()` instead of cloning the whole `Type` would lose path qualifiers and fail.
- **Name-only classification at 047, no type-based override.** The progress note in the new test `body_field_classification_does_not_depend_on_type` pins the behavior: even if a user writes `body: Request`, 047 classifies it as `Body`. This might seem wrong (the spec's parenthetical "not Request, not QueryParams" suggests a type-based exclusion) but the right place for that precedence rule is 048/049, where the Request/QueryParams TYPE matchers exist. 047's job is "this field is named `body` → it's a body candidate"; if the type makes that nonsensical, 048/049 can override (or rustc can fail at the codegen site). Pinning the name-only behavior here makes any future precedence-rule change explicit (the test will need to be updated, which is the right friction).
- **No new public observables in the marker const.** Considered emitting `pub const __JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_BODY_FIELD: Option<&'static str> = Some("body")` so the integration test could assert detection. Rejected because (a) 046's progress note explicitly argued against emitting field names/kinds publicly — they commit to a public surface that 051+ replaces; (b) the unit tests on `parse_auto_middleware_input` directly verify kind classification, which is sufficient parse-witness; (c) integration tests should test through public APIs, not macro-internal observables. The integration test in `jolt-core/tests/auto_middleware_derive.rs` stays unchanged at 047 (it still just asserts `__JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT` values; the body field's kind is unit-tested in the macro crate).
- **Shared `classify_field` helper rather than inline match in `parse_struct_fields`.** Three lines of code today, but the indirection pays off when 048/049 extend the rule: `classify_field(ident)` becomes `classify_field(ident, ty)` (taking both parameters), and the type-based matching for `QueryParams<T>` and `Request` lives there alongside the name-based matching for `body`. A future refactor to a struct of (name_predicate, type_predicate) -> kind tuples can replace the function body without touching `parse_struct_fields`. Premature abstraction concern: yes, but the function is single-purpose and the rule is going to grow predictably across 048/049/050.
- **Test surface: 7 new unit tests in `mod auto_middleware::tests`.** Pin: (a) PRD-mandated `body: CreateUserRequest → Body` (type round-trip included); (b) primitive `body: String → Body` (proves name-based, not type-based); (c) `count: usize → Other` (non-body fall-through); (d) mixed-struct with body in middle position → only the body field is `Body`; (e) ordering-independence — body at first vs. last position; (f) unit struct yields zero body-fields (filter-iter contract for 053); (g) `body: Request` STILL classifies as Body (pins name-only rule, makes any future precedence change explicit). Total `mod auto_middleware::tests` count: 10 → 17.

Files changed:
- `jolt-macros/src/auto_middleware.rs` — added `FieldKind` enum (`Body`, `Other`); added `kind: FieldKind` field to `AutoMiddlewareField`; added `classify_field(ident: &Ident) -> FieldKind` helper; updated `parse_struct_fields` to call `classify_field` per named field; updated module docstring to mark 047 landed and document the name-based rule; added 7 unit tests under `mod tests`.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-047 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- **JOLT-RS-048 (priority 48, phase10): "Detect query_params fields: field typed QueryParams<T> or HashMap<String, String>. Mark for query extraction."** Builds directly on 047's `FieldKind`. The detection rule will need TYPE inspection (unlike 047's name-only rule): match on the type's last path segment being `QueryParams` (for `QueryParams<T>`) or the full path being `HashMap<String, String>` / `std::collections::HashMap<String, String>` (for the explicit map shape). The `classify_field` helper signature should grow a `ty: &Type` parameter; the body-detection name match stays first (since the spec says "if `body: T` field exists" without type qualifications). A reasonable precedence: `QueryParams<T>` typed → `QueryParams` kind regardless of name; `HashMap<String, String>` typed AND named `query_params` → `QueryParams` kind; `body`-named → `Body` kind; else `Other`. The `query_params: QueryParams<Filters>` case in the existing `parses_struct_with_various_field_types` test will break when 048 lands — flag for update.
- **JOLT-RS-049 (priority 49, phase10): "Detect Request reference fields: field typed &Request or Request. Mark for req injection."** Parallel to 048 but matches `&Request` / `Request` types. The `req: &'a Request` case in the existing `parses_struct_with_various_field_types` test will break similarly.
- **JOLT-RS-050 (priority 50, phase10): "Detect #[cors] attribute on the struct itself."** Different shape: parses `input.attrs`, not field types. Add `pub cors: bool` (or `pub cors_attr: Option<CorsAttr>` if 050+ wants config) to `AutoMiddlewareInput`. The current parser drops `input.attrs` on the floor.
- **`parses_struct_with_various_field_types` test in `mod auto_middleware::tests` will need updates as 048/049 land.** Current expectation: all five fields get `Other` kind (since 047 only classifies `body`-named fields). When 048 adds QueryParams matching, the `query_params: QueryParams<Filters>` and `headers: std::collections::HashMap<String, String>` fields' classifications will shift. When 049 adds Request matching, `req: &'a Request` will shift. The test currently asserts only field count and names; if it grows kind assertions in 048/049, update accordingly.
- **`jolt-core/tests/auto_middleware_derive.rs` integration test stays unchanged at 047.** Still asserts only `__JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT`; the `body: CreateUserRequest` field in `MixedMiddleware` is now classified as `Body` internally but there's no public observable to assert against. When 053's body-extraction codegen lands, the integration test will exercise the extraction (post a JSON body, assert the middleware's `body` field gets populated).
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test).** Still the only pre-046 holdouts. 045 is mostly satisfied by 044's existing `into_router_serves_*` tests. 027/032 remain pure test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies.
- **`generate_dispatch_match` still has `#[allow(dead_code)]` and is unused.** Decision deferred from 043 + 044 + 046: keep or delete. No pending consumer; recommend deletion in a tracker-item cleanup pass.
- **`mod auto_middleware::tests` is now at 17 tests.** Well below the ~25 split-by-concern threshold flagged in 040-046's progress notes; no organizational changes needed yet. Will likely cross the threshold around 050 (when struct-attr parsing adds another 5-10 tests).
- **`mod endpoint::tests` still at 59 tests.** The split-by-concern recommendation from 043/044/046's progress notes still stands; not blocking anything but worth doing as a tracker cleanup item.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-048: query-params FieldKind classification

PRD item: JOLT-RS-048 (priority 48, phase10-automiddleware-field-parsing) — "Detect query_params fields: field typed QueryParams<T> or HashMap<String, String>. Mark for query extraction." Verification: "Unit test: field query: QueryParams<Filters> → detected as query field."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 048 extends the `FieldKind` enum and commits the precedence rule (type-based QueryParams beats name-based body) that 049 will compose on top of. It commits to (a) type-before-name precedence, pinned by `query_params_type_takes_precedence_over_body_name` so 049 can't accidentally re-order without a test failure; (b) name-based detection requiring BOTH the right name AND the right type for the HashMap shape (rejecting `headers: HashMap<String, String>` as Other), pinned by `hashmap_string_string_with_non_query_params_name_classifies_as_other`; (c) last-path-segment matching for both `QueryParams` and `HashMap` (covers bare and path-qualified forms uniformly). All three decisions are load-bearing for 049/053. 027/032/045 remain pure test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase10+ work.

Verification:
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 111 jolt-core unit + 8 jolt-core inventory_registration integration + 2 jolt-core auto_middleware_derive integration + 76 jolt-macros unit (was 66; +10 new tests for 048) = 197 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`, documented in 043's progress notes); 0 new warnings.
- The PRD-mandated "Unit test: field query: QueryParams<Filters> → detected as query field" is satisfied by `parses_query_params_typed_field_as_query_params_kind` in `jolt-macros/src/auto_middleware.rs`'s `mod tests`. The test parses `struct WithQuery { query: QueryParams<Filters> }`, asserts `parsed.fields[0].kind == FieldKind::QueryParams`, and verifies the type round-trips through tokenization (so 053's typed query-extraction codegen will have the right tokens). The field name `query` (NOT `query_params`) is intentional — it pins that the type-based rule fires regardless of name, satisfying the PRD verification literally.

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..047 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory). Cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **Type-before-name precedence in `classify_field`.** The 047 progress notes recommended "QueryParams<T> typed → QueryParams kind regardless of name; HashMap<String, String> typed AND named query_params → QueryParams kind; body-named → Body kind; else Other". Implemented exactly that order. The reason matters: a hypothetical `body: QueryParams<T>` is QueryParams, NOT Body, because the type's framework-meaning (extraction from query string) overrides the name's framework-meaning (extraction from body). Pinned by `query_params_type_takes_precedence_over_body_name`. The reverse precedence (name first) would have been simpler to reason about per-rule, but worse for the user — calling a `QueryParams<T>` field `body` is almost certainly a typo, and the type-first rule produces correct extraction in that case rather than calling `__req.json::<QueryParams<T>>()` (which serde_json wouldn't know how to deserialize because QueryParams isn't a JSON-shaped type).
- **HashMap rule requires BOTH the right name AND the right type.** Considered three shapes: (a) name-only (`query_params: T` for any T → QueryParams) — rejected because the type tells codegen what extraction call to emit; without a type constraint, codegen would have to guess between `QueryParams<T>` and `HashMap<String, String>` extraction shapes; (b) type-only (`HashMap<String, String>` for any name → QueryParams) — rejected because then `headers: HashMap<String, String>` would silently get query-string extraction, which is wrong (headers come from request headers, not query params); (c) name AND type (current choice) — clear, narrow, and the user-facing error is helpful: a user who writes `headers: HashMap<String, String>` and expected query extraction will see Other (Default::default()) at runtime, which they can debug by either renaming to `query_params` or switching to `QueryParams<T>`. Pinned by `hashmap_string_string_with_non_query_params_name_classifies_as_other`.
- **`type_path_ends_with` matches on the LAST path segment, not the full path.** Three considered shapes: (a) string-compare against the full quoted form (e.g. `"QueryParams"` and `"crate::api::QueryParams"`) — rejected because it commits to a specific path and forces every test to write the exact form; (b) match on segments[0] (the first ident) — rejected because `crate::api::QueryParams<T>` has segments[0] == `crate`; (c) match on segments.last() (current) — covers bare `QueryParams<T>`, `crate::api::QueryParams<T>`, and `::framework::QueryParams<T>` uniformly. Pinned by `parses_path_qualified_query_params_as_query_params_kind`. The same rule applies to `HashMap` (covers `std::collections::HashMap` and bare `HashMap`) and reuses the helper for the `String` value-type check. 049 will reuse `type_path_ends_with` for `Request` matching.
- **`is_hashmap_string_string` does NOT match `HashMap<String, u32>` or other non-String value types.** The framework's framework-meaning for `query_params` is the raw-map shape (string keys, string values, no typed deserialization). A `HashMap<String, u32>` named `query_params` falls through to Other — the user probably meant `QueryParams<T>` for typed extraction, and forcing them to either rename the field or switch to the typed shape is the right friction. Pinned by `named_query_params_with_non_string_value_hashmap_classifies_as_other`.
- **`type_path_ends_with` also doesn't match `&QueryParams<T>` or `QueryParams<T>::Inner`.** A reference type is `Type::Reference`, not `Type::Path` — the `let Type::Path(tp) = ty else { ... }` early-return discards it. This matters because 049 will detect `&Request` separately (different syn AST node), and the QueryParams rule should NOT fire on `&QueryParams<T>` (it's a different shape — pre-borrowed, no extraction needed). Tested implicitly by virtue of the existing `body_field_classification_does_not_depend_on_type` test continuing to pass with `body: Request` (which is a Path, not a Reference; the test doesn't exercise & vs no-& but the codepath is the same).
- **Did NOT add a dedicated `is_query_params_type` helper alongside `type_path_ends_with`.** The single helper handles both `QueryParams` and (eventually, for 049) `Request` matching on the last-segment-ident shape. A dedicated `is_query_params_type` helper would be three lines of indirection over a single `type_path_ends_with(ty, "QueryParams")` call. The framework-name strings (`"QueryParams"`, `"HashMap"`, `"String"`, and 049's `"Request"`) are short enough that inlining them at the call site doesn't hurt readability. 050 will need a different helper (struct-attr inspection, not type matching) so the helpers don't compose into a unified machine.
- **Existing `parses_struct_with_various_field_types` test left as-is — still asserts only count and names.** The test was kept loose in 047 for exactly this kind of incremental add. With 048's classification rules, the test's `query_params: QueryParams<Filters>` field is now classified as QueryParams (rule 1: type-based) and `headers: std::collections::HashMap<String, String>` stays Other (HashMap rule requires `query_params` name). Both pass the existing `count == 5` and name-list assertions. A NEW test (`classifies_all_three_kinds_in_mixed_struct`) covers the kind classification for an end-to-end mixed struct. Keeping the existing test shape prevents 049 from having to re-update it again when Request matching lands.
- **Test surface: 10 new unit tests in `mod auto_middleware::tests`.** Pin: (a) PRD-mandated `query: QueryParams<Filters> → QueryParams` (with type round-trip); (b) `q: crate::api::QueryParams<T>` → QueryParams (path qualification); (c) `query_params: HashMap<String, String>` → QueryParams (rule 2, bare HashMap); (d) `query_params: std::collections::HashMap<String, String>` → QueryParams (rule 2, path-qualified HashMap); (e) `headers: HashMap<String, String>` → Other (HashMap rule requires query_params name); (f) `query_params: HashMap<String, u32>` → Other (HashMap rule requires String value type); (g) `body: QueryParams<T>` → QueryParams (type-before-name precedence); (h) `query_params: Vec<String>` → Other (the field name alone isn't sufficient); (i) unit struct → zero QueryParams fields (filter-iter contract for 053); (j) end-to-end mixed struct with Body + QueryParams + Other kinds in correct order. Total `mod auto_middleware::tests` count: 17 → 27.

Files changed:
- `jolt-macros/src/auto_middleware.rs` — added `QueryParams` variant to `FieldKind`; extended `classify_field` to take `ty: &Type` and apply the type-based + name+type rules in precedence order; added `type_path_ends_with(ty, name)` and `is_hashmap_string_string(ty)` helpers; updated `FieldKind` and module-level rustdoc to document the precedence rules; added 10 unit tests under `mod tests`. Imported `GenericArgument` and `PathArguments` from `syn`.
- `jolt-macros/src/lib.rs` — updated the `auto_middleware_derive` rustdoc to mark 047 + 048 as landed.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-048 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- **JOLT-RS-049 (priority 49, phase10): "Detect Request reference fields: field typed &Request or Request. Mark for req injection."** Now has stable `FieldKind` and `type_path_ends_with` helper to build on. The detection rule will need to handle BOTH `Type::Path` (for the bare `Request`) and `Type::Reference` (for `&Request`, `&'a Request`, `&mut Request`). Two implementation paths: (a) extend `type_path_ends_with` to peel through `Type::Reference` to its inner type before doing the path match — clean, but changes 048's existing behavior (a `&QueryParams<T>` field would suddenly classify as QueryParams, which may or may not be desired for codegen); (b) add a separate `is_request_type` helper that explicitly handles both Type::Path and Type::Reference cases — preserves 048's strict "no references" behavior. (b) is recommended; the "extract by reference" semantics are different from "extract by value" enough that they deserve separate detection. 049 should also add a `Request` variant to `FieldKind`. The existing `body_field_classification_does_not_depend_on_type` test will need updating: `body: Request` is currently Body (because Request type is neither QueryParams nor HashMap, so the body-name rule fires); 049's precedence rule should decide whether type-Request beats name-body. Recommend type-before-name (consistent with 048's QueryParams precedence): `body: Request` → Request. Update the test accordingly when 049 lands.

After 050, `mod auto_middleware::tests` will likely cross the ~25 split-by-concern threshold (currently at 27); split into `mod parse_struct_shape` + `mod classify_field_kind` + `mod expand_emission` + `mod struct_attrs_cors`.
- **`parses_struct_with_various_field_types` test in `mod auto_middleware::tests` still doesn't assert kinds.** Deliberately left loose for 049's update — when Request matching lands, the `req: &'a Request` field will shift to FieldKind::Request. If the test grows kind assertions then, all five fields' kinds become assertable; do it as part of 049 to consolidate the kind-classification surface.
- **`type_path_ends_with` will likely grow into a public-or-pub(crate) `match_path_segment` helper across the macro crate.** 049 reuses it for `Request`; 050 doesn't (struct-attr inspection); 051+ probably reuses it for trait-bound matching (e.g. detecting `T: DeserializeOwned` if the macro ever does compile-time trait inference). Currently `pub(crate)` in `auto_middleware.rs`; if `endpoint.rs` ever needs the same helper (e.g. for return-type inspection in 040's signature validation), promote it to a sibling module like `jolt-macros/src/types.rs`. Out of scope until there's a second consumer; flag-worthy at 049's close.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test).** Still the only pre-046 holdouts. 045 is mostly satisfied by 044's existing `into_router_serves_*` tests. 027/032 remain pure test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies.

## 2026-05-10 — JOLT-RS-049: request-injection FieldKind classification

PRD item: JOLT-RS-049 (priority 49, phase10-automiddleware-field-parsing) — "Detect Request reference fields: field typed &Request or Request. Mark for req injection." Verification: "Unit test: field req: &Request → detected as request injection."

Why picked over the strict-priority next items (JOLT-RS-027 port-binding-conflict polish; JOLT-RS-032 endpoint-registry test bundle; JOLT-RS-045 endpoint-integration polish): per the auto-prompt's prioritization rule ("architectural decisions and core abstractions" first), 049 closes the kind-classification surface that 047/048 opened — adding the third type-based variant (`FieldKind::Request`) and committing the by-reference-handling pattern (`Type::Reference` peeling) that 053's codegen will dispatch on. The decision points pinned this iteration are load-bearing for 053's per-field extraction code: (a) shared-only references (`&Request` / `&'a Request`) match; mutable references (`&mut Request`) explicitly do NOT match, narrowing the surface to the spec's read-only injection contract; (b) bare `Request` (by-value) matches too, but the by-value vs by-ref distinction is preserved on `AutoMiddlewareField.ty` so codegen can emit the right call shape; (c) Request rule lives between QueryParams and the body-name rule, so `body: &Request` classifies as Request — type-before-name precedence consistent with 048's QueryParams behavior. 027/032/045 remain pure test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies; deferring them does not block any phase10+ work.

Verification:
- `cargo check --workspace` → clean.
- `cargo test --workspace` → 111 jolt-core unit + 8 jolt-core inventory_registration integration + 2 jolt-core auto_middleware_derive integration + 85 jolt-macros unit (was 76; +9 new tests for 049) = 206 tests pass; no regressions in any sibling crate.
- `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets` → same 2 pre-existing baseline warnings (`new_without_default` on `RequestExt` and `JoltServer`, documented in 043's progress notes); 0 new warnings.
- The PRD-mandated "Unit test: field req: &Request → detected as request injection" is satisfied by `parses_request_reference_field_as_request_kind` in `jolt-macros/src/auto_middleware.rs`'s `mod tests`. The test parses `struct WithReq { req: &Request }`, asserts `parsed.fields[0].kind == FieldKind::Request`, and verifies the type round-trips through tokenization (so 053's injection codegen will have the right tokens to splice back into the per-request call).

Note on harness instructions: same as JOLT-RS-007..048 — the auto-prompt's `npm run type-check` / Bun-Hono server commands don't apply (no `package.json`, no `server/` directory). Cargo is the verification tool.

Key decisions:
- **`is_request_type` peels `Type::Reference` to its inner type, then reuses `type_path_ends_with(inner, "Request")`.** Two implementation paths considered, both flagged in 048's progress notes: (a) extend `type_path_ends_with` itself to peel-and-match references — rejected because it changes 048's existing behavior (a `&QueryParams<T>` field would suddenly classify as QueryParams, which is wrong: a pre-borrowed `&QueryParams<T>` has different extraction semantics from a by-value `QueryParams<T>`, and the user almost certainly meant something else); (b) add a separate `is_request_type` helper that explicitly handles both Type::Path and Type::Reference cases — preserves 048's strict no-references-for-QueryParams behavior, and keeps reference-handling local to the rule that needs it. Picked (b). The helper is 6 lines; if 050+ ever adds another reference-aware rule, the peel logic can be extracted into a shared `peel_shared_ref(ty: &Type) -> &Type` helper, but it's premature today.
- **Mutability disqualifies: `&mut Request` falls through to Other.** Three considered shapes: (a) match all references regardless of mutability — rejected because the spec's middleware injection is shared-reference (`&Request`); a `&mut Request` field implies the user wants exclusive access to mutate the request, which is not what the framework provides; (b) match only shared refs, mut refs fall through (current choice) — narrows the surface to what the spec actually supports; (c) reject mut refs with a compile_error (different behavior from "other") — rejected because the user might have a legitimate non-injection use case for a `&mut Request` field on a middleware struct, and forcing them to rename it to avoid the rule is wrong friction. Picked (b). Pinned by `mut_request_reference_classifies_as_other`. The progress note in the test makes any future relaxation explicit (the test will need to be updated, which is the right friction).
- **`Option<Request>` falls through to Other.** The integration test in `auto_middleware_derive.rs` uses `req: Option<Request>`, and that field needs to STAY Other for backwards compatibility with 046's `MixedMiddleware.__JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT == 6` assertion (which is shape-agnostic but the integration test exists specifically to exercise the "various field types" surface, including `Option<Request>` as a wrapped framework type that does NOT trigger injection). The last-path-segment matcher handles this correctly: `Option<Request>` has last path segment `Option`, not `Request` — `type_path_ends_with(ty, "Request")` returns false. Pinned by `option_request_classifies_as_other`. If a future PRD wants `Option<Request>` to ALSO trigger injection (with a `None` outcome being meaningful), the rule needs to grow generic-arg inspection — not in scope for 049.
- **Type-before-name precedence: `body: Request` is Request (replaces 047's name-only behavior).** 048's progress notes explicitly recommended this: "`body: Request` is currently Body (because Request type is neither QueryParams nor HashMap, so the body-name rule fires); 049's precedence rule should decide whether type-Request beats name-body. Recommend type-before-name (consistent with 048's QueryParams precedence)." Implemented exactly that. The same reasoning applies as for QueryParams: a `Request`-typed field named `body` is almost certainly a typo, and the type-first rule produces correct injection rather than a body-extraction call (which would call `__req.json::<Request>()` and fail because `Request` doesn't impl `DeserializeOwned`). Pinned by `request_type_takes_precedence_over_body_name` (replaces 047's `body_field_classification_does_not_depend_on_type` test) and `request_reference_takes_precedence_over_body_name` (parallel pin for `body: &Request`). The replaced test was a 047-era pin of name-only classification; with 049 narrowing the rule, the replacement is the correct shape.
- **Field-name irrelevant when the type matches.** Parallel to 048's QueryParams behavior: a field NAMED `whatever` typed `&Request` still classifies as Request, ensuring codegen picks up injection regardless of the user's chosen name. Pinned by `request_classification_does_not_depend_on_field_name`. The naming convention `req` is informal; the type is canonical.
- **Path qualification covered uniformly via last-path-segment matching.** `&Request`, `&::jolt_core::Request`, `crate::Request`, `&framework::request::Request` all classify as Request. The same `type_path_ends_with` helper that 048 uses for QueryParams handles the inner type in `is_request_type`. Pinned by `parses_path_qualified_request_as_request_kind` (covers both bare-path `::jolt_core::Request` and reference-path `&crate::Request`).
- **Did NOT extract a `peel_shared_ref` shared helper.** The peel logic in `is_request_type` is 4 lines; extracting it to a sibling helper just to call it once would add an indirection over a clear inline match. If 050 needs reference-peeling for struct-attr handling (it won't — struct attrs are on `DeriveInput.attrs`, not field types), or if 051+ adds another by-ref rule, promote the helper then. Out of scope until there's a second consumer.
- **Existing test `parses_struct_with_various_field_types` still doesn't assert kinds.** Deliberately left loose since 047 — the test covers field count + names. With 049's classification rules, the `req: &'a Request` field is now `Request` and `query_params: QueryParams<Filters>` is `QueryParams` (already covered by 048's tests separately), but the existing test stays untouched. A new test, `classifies_all_four_kinds_in_mixed_struct` (rename from 048's `classifies_all_three_kinds_in_mixed_struct`), pins the kind sequence end-to-end in field order.
- **Test surface: 9 new unit tests in `mod auto_middleware::tests` (76 → 85), plus 2 renamed/updated tests.** Pin: (a) PRD-mandated `req: &Request → Request` (with type round-trip); (b) bare `req: Request → Request`; (c) `req: &'a Request → Request` (lifetime annotation); (d) path-qualified `req: ::jolt_core::Request` and `&crate::Request → Request`; (e) name irrelevance — `whatever: &'a Request → Request`; (f) `&mut Request → Other` (mut refs explicitly excluded); (g) `Option<Request> → Other` (wrapped types not matched); (h) unit struct → no Request fields (filter-iter contract for 053); (i) `body: &'a Request → Request` (precedence pin for by-ref). Renamed: `body_field_classification_does_not_depend_on_type` → `request_type_takes_precedence_over_body_name` (asserts the reversed outcome under 049). Renamed: `classifies_all_three_kinds_in_mixed_struct` → `classifies_all_four_kinds_in_mixed_struct` (now asserts Request kind on `req: Request`). Total `mod auto_middleware::tests` count: 27 → 36.

Files changed:
- `jolt-macros/src/auto_middleware.rs` — added `Request` variant to `FieldKind`; added `is_request_type` helper handling `Type::Path` (bare) and shared-only `Type::Reference` (mutability check); inserted Request rule in `classify_field` between QueryParams and the name-based rules (type-before-name precedence); updated `FieldKind` and module-level rustdoc to document the new rule + precedence; added 9 new unit tests under `mod tests`; renamed 2 existing tests to reflect the new outcomes (`body_field_classification_does_not_depend_on_type` → `request_type_takes_precedence_over_body_name`; `classifies_all_three_kinds_in_mixed_struct` → `classifies_all_four_kinds_in_mixed_struct`).
- `jolt-macros/src/lib.rs` — updated the `auto_middleware_derive` rustdoc to mark 049 as landed.
- `prd.json` — JOLT-RS-049 passes: true.

Notes for next iterations:
- **JOLT-RS-050 (priority 50, phase10): "Detect #[cors] attribute on the struct itself."** Different shape from 047-049: parses `input.attrs` instead of field types. Add `pub cors: bool` (or `pub cors_attr: Option<CorsAttr>` if 050+ wants config) to `AutoMiddlewareInput`. The current parser drops `input.attrs` on the floor — `parse_auto_middleware_input` only consumes `input.ident` and `input.data`. Add a `parse_struct_attrs(attrs: &[Attribute]) -> bool` helper alongside the existing `parse_struct_fields`. After 050 lands, `mod auto_middleware::tests` will be at ~41 tests (36 + ~5 for attr parsing); past the ~25 split-by-concern threshold for sure.
- **JOLT-RS-051-053 (phase10 close).** With kind classification complete (047/048/049), 051+ generates the actual `tower::Layer` impl that consumes `parsed.fields.iter()` and dispatches per `kind`. The `Other` catch-all becomes `Default::default()` per-request; `Body` becomes `__req.json::<#ty>()`; `QueryParams` becomes the typed-or-raw-map extraction; `Request` becomes the per-request injection (clone for by-value, borrow for by-ref). The `__JOLT_AUTO_MIDDLEWARE_FIELD_COUNT` marker const can be removed at that point; the integration test in `auto_middleware_derive.rs` will need to change to assert layer behavior rather than the marker const.
- **`AutoMiddlewareField.ty` is the by-value vs by-ref witness for codegen.** A regression that called `is_request_type` on the field's type and then wrote the kind to `FieldKind::Request` without preserving the original ty would lose the by-ref info — codegen in 053 would not know whether to emit `req.clone()` (for bare `Request`) or `&*req_ref` (for `&Request`). Pinned implicitly by the per-test `quote!(#ty).to_string()` round-trip in `parses_request_reference_field_as_request_kind`. If a future refactor changes the parsed-shape storage, ensure the original `Type` is still available.
- **`type_path_ends_with` now has 2 consumers (QueryParams via 048 and Request via 049 through `is_request_type`).** The "second consumer" threshold for a shared-helpers module (flagged in 048's progress notes) is met, but the helper is still small and `pub(crate)` in `auto_middleware.rs`. Promotion to `jolt-macros/src/types.rs` only makes sense if `endpoint.rs` ever needs the same helper (e.g. for return-type inspection in 040's signature validation, which currently does its own type matching). Out of scope for 049+; flag-worthy if signature-validation gets a refactor.
- **JOLT-RS-027 (port-binding-conflict polish), 032 (endpoint-registry test bundle), 045 (endpoint-integration test).** Still the only pre-046 holdouts. 045 is mostly satisfied by 044's existing `into_router_serves_*` tests. 027/032 remain pure test-bundle polish with no upstream dependencies.
- **`generate_dispatch_match` still has `#[allow(dead_code)]` and is unused.** Decision deferred from 043 + 044 + 046 + 047 + 048: keep or delete. No pending consumer. Recommend deletion in a tracker-item cleanup pass after phase10 closes.
- **`mod auto_middleware::tests` is now at 36 tests** (was 27 after 048). Well past the ~25 split-by-concern threshold. Recommended split when 050 closes: `mod parse_struct_shape` (named/unit/tuple/enum/union acceptance, ~8 tests) + `mod classify_field_kind` (kind classification per field, ~22 tests covering body/query/request rules + precedence) + `mod expand_emission` (TokenStream output shape, ~6 tests) + `mod struct_attrs_cors` (050's struct-level attr parsing, ~5 tests). Purely organizational; not blocking any PRD item.
